href="#FAQ-bootstrap">\n      Loading Bootstrapped Models\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#FAQ-extending">\n      Extending Backbone\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#FAQ-mvc">\n      Traditional MVC\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#FAQ-this">\n      Binding "this"\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n  <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-todos">\n      Todos\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-documentcloud">\n      DocumentCloud\n     </a>\n   IRCCloud\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-pitchfork">\n      Pitchfork\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-spin">\n      Spin\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-zocdoc">\n      ZocDoc\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-walmart">\n      Walmart Mobile\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-groupon">\n      Groupon Now!\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-basecamp">\n      Basecamp\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-slavery-footprint">\n      Slavery Footprint\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-stripe">\n      Stripe\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-airbnb">\n      Airbnb\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-cloudapp">\n      CloudApp\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-seatgeek">\n      SeatGeek\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-easel">\n      Easel\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     -\n     <a href="#examples-jolicloud">\n      Jolicloud\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-salon">\n      Salon.io\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-tilemill">\n      TileMill\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-blossom">\n      Blossom\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-trello">\n      Trello\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-tzigla">\n      Tzigla\n     </a>\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   <a class="toc_title" href="#changelog">\n    Change Log\n   </a>\n  </div>\n  <div class="container">\n   <p>\n    <img alt="Backbone.js" id="logo" src="docs/images/backbone.png"/>\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Backbone.js gives structure to web applications\n      by providing\n    <b>\n     models\n    </b>\n    with key-value binding and custom events,\n    <b>\n     collections\n    </b>\n    with a rich API of enumerable functions,\n    <b>\n     views\n    </b>\n    with declarative event handling, and connects it all to your\n      existing API over a RESTful JSON interface.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The project is\n    <a href="http://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/">\n     hosted on GitHub\n    </a>\n    ,\n      and the\n    <a href="docs/backbone.html">\n     annotated source code\n    </a>\n    is available,\n      as well as an online\n    <a href="test/">\n     test suite\n    </a>\n    ,\n      an\n    <a href="examples/todos/index.html">\n     example application\n    </a>\n    ,\n      a\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/wiki/Tutorials%2C-blog-posts-and-example-sites">\n     list of tutorials\n    </a>\n    and a\n    <a href="#examples">\n     long list of real-world projects\n    </a>\n    that use Backbone.\n      Backbone is available for use under the\n    <a href="http://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/blob/master/LICENSE">\n     MIT software license\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    You can report bugs and discuss features on the\n    <a href="http://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/issues">\n     GitHub issues page\n    </a>\n    ,\n      on Freenode IRC in the\n    <tt>\n     #documentcloud\n    </tt>\n    channel, post questions to the\n    <a href="https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/backbonejs">\n     Google Group\n    </a>\n    ,\n      add pages to the\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/wiki">\n     wiki\n    </a>\n    or send tweets to\n    <a href="http://twitter.com/documentcloud">\n     @documentcloud\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <i>\n     Backbone is an open-source component of\n     <a href="http://documentcloud.org/">\n      DocumentCloud\n     </a>\n     .\n    </i>\n   </p>\n   <h2 id="downloads">\n    Downloads &amp; Dependencies\n    <span class="interface" style="padding-left: 7px; font-size:11px; font-weight: normal;">\n     (Right-click, and use "Save As")\n    </span>\n   </h2>\n   <table>\n    <tbody>\n     <tr>\n      <td>\n       <a class="punch" href="backbone.js">\n        Development Version (1.1.2)\n       </a>\n      </td>\n      <td class="text">\n       <i>\n        60kb, Full source, tons of comments\n       </i>\n      </td>\n     </tr>\n     <tr>\n      <td>\n       <a class="punch" href="backbone-min.js">\n        Production Version (1.1.2)\n       </a>\n      </td>\n      <td class="text" style="line-height: 16px;">\n       <i>\n        6.5kb, Packed and gzipped\n       </i>\n       <br/>\n       <small>\n        (\n        <a href="backbone-min.map">\n         Source Map\n        </a>\n        )\n       </small>\n      </td>\n     </tr>\n     <tr>\n      <td>\n       <a class="punch" href="https://raw.github.com/jashkenas/backbone/master/backbone.js">\n        Edge Version (master)\n       </a>\n      </td>\n      <td>\n       <i>\n        Unreleased, use at your own risk\n       </i>\n       <a class="travis-badge" href="https://travis-ci.org/jashkenas/backbone">\n        <img src="https://travis-ci.org/jashkenas/backbone.png"/>\n       </a>\n      </td>\n     </tr>\n    </tbody>\n   </table>\n   <p>\n    Backbone\'s only hard dependency is\n    <a href="http://underscorejs.org/">\n     Underscore.js\n    </a>\n    <small>\n     ( &gt;= 1.5.0)\n    </small>\n    .\n      For RESTful persistence, history support via\n    <a href="#Router">\n     Backbone.Router\n    </a>\n    and DOM manipulation with\n    <a href="#View">\n     Backbone.View\n    </a>\n    , include\n    <b>\n     <a href="http://jquery.com">\n      jQuery\n     </a>\n    </b>\n    , and\n    <b>\n     <a href="https://github.com/douglascrockford/JSON-js">\n      json2.js\n     </a>\n    </b>\n    for older\n      Internet Explorer support.\n    <i>\n     (Mimics of the Underscore and jQuery APIs, such as\n     <a href="http://lodash.com">\n      Lo-Dash\n     </a>\n     and\n     <a href="http://zeptojs.com">\n      Zepto\n     </a>\n     , will\n      also tend to work, with varying degrees of compatibility.)\n    </i>\n   </p>\n   <h2 id="introduction">\n    Introduction\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    When working on a web application that involves a lot of JavaScript, one\n      of the first things you learn is to stop tying your data to the DOM. It\'s all\n      too easy to create JavaScript applications that end up as tangled piles of\n      jQuery selectors and callbacks, all trying frantically to keep data in\n      sync between the HTML UI, your JavaScript logic, and the database on your\n      server. For rich client-side applications, a more structured approach\n      is often helpful.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    With Backbone, you represent your data as\n    <a href="#Model">\n     Models\n    </a>\n    , which can be created, validated, destroyed,\n      and saved to the server. Whenever a UI action causes an attribute of\n      a model to change, the model triggers a\n    <i>\n     "change"\n    </i>\n    event; all\n      the\n    <a href="#View">\n     Views\n    </a>\n    that display the model\'s state can be notified of the\n      change, so that they are able to respond accordingly, re-rendering themselves with\n      the new information. In a finished Backbone app, you don\'t have to write the glue\n      code that looks into the DOM to find an element with a specific\n    <i>\n     id\n    </i>\n    ,\n      and update the HTML manually\n      \xe2\x80\x94 when the model changes, the views simply update themselves.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Philosophically, Backbone is an attempt to discover the minimal set\n      of data-structuring (models and collections) and user interface (views\n      and URLs) primitives that are generally useful when building web applications with\n      JavaScript. In an ecosystem where overarching, decides-everything-for-you\n      frameworks are commonplace, and many libraries require your site to be\n      reorganized to suit their look, feel, and default behavior \xe2\x80\x94 Backbone should\n      continue to be a tool that gives you the\n    <i>\n     freedom\n    </i>\n    to design the full\n      experience of your web application.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    If you\'re new here, and aren\'t yet quite sure what Backbone is for, start by\n      browsing the\n    <a href="#examples">\n     list of Backbone-based projects\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Many of the examples that follow are runnable. Click the\n    <i>\n     play\n    </i>\n    button\n      to execute them.\n   </p>\n   <h2 id="upgrading">\n    Upgrading to 1.1\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    Backbone\n    <b>\n     1.1\n    </b>\n    should be a fairly painless upgrade from the\n    <b>\n     0.9.X\n    </b>\n    series. If you\'re upgrading from an older version, be sure to check out the\n    <a href="#changelog">\n     change log\n    </a>\n    . In brief, a few of the larger breaking\n      changes are:\n   </p>\n   <ul>\n    <li>\n     If you want to smartly update the contents of a Collection,\n        adding new models, removing missing ones, and merging those already present,\n        you now call\n     <a href="#Collection-set">\n      set\n     </a>\n     (previously named "update"),\n        a similar operation to calling\n     <tt>\n      set\n     </tt>\n     on a Model. This is now the\n        default when you call\n     <a href="#Collection-fetch">\n      fetch\n     </a>\n     on a collection.\n        To get the old behavior, pass\n     <tt>\n      {reset: true}\n     </tt>\n     .\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     If you have characters in your URL segments that require URL encoding,\n        Backbone will now decode them for you (normalizing the behavior\n        cross-browser) before your route handlers receive them as arguments.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     In\n     <b>\n      0.9.x\n     </b>\n     , Backbone events gained two new methods:\n     <a href="#Events-listenTo">\n      listenTo\n     </a>\n     and\n     <a href="#Events-stopListening">\n      stopListening\n     </a>\n     , which make it easier\n        to create Views that have all of their observers unbound when you\n        want to\n     <a href="#View-remove">\n      remove\n     </a>\n     the view.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     Model validation is now only enforced by default in\n     <a href="#Model-save">\n      save\n     </a>\n     \xe2\x80\x94 not in\n     <a href="#Model-set">\n      set\n     </a>\n     unless the\n     <tt>\n      {validate:true}\n     </tt>\n     option is passed. Model validation now fires an\n     <tt>\n      "invalid"\n     </tt>\n     event instead of\n     <tt>\n      "error"\n     </tt>\n     .\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     In 1.1, Backbone Views no longer have the\n     <tt>\n      options\n     </tt>\n     argument\n        attached as\n     <tt>\n      this.options\n     </tt>\n     automatically. Feel free to continue\n        attaching it if you like.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     In 1.1, The\n     <b>\n      Collection\n     </b>\n     methods\n     <tt>\n      add\n     </tt>\n     ,\n     <tt>\n      remove\n     </tt>\n     ,\n     <tt>\n      set\n     </tt>\n     ,\n     <tt>\n      push\n     </tt>\n     , and\n     <tt>\n      shift\n     </tt>\n     now return the model\n        (or models) added or removed from the collection.\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   <h2 id="Events">\n    Backbone.Events\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     Events\n    </b>\n    is a module that can be mixed in to any object, giving the\n      object the ability to bind and trigger custom named events. Events do not\n      have to be declared before they are bound, and may take passed arguments.\n      For example:\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var object = {};\n\n_.extend(object, Backbone.Events);\n\nobject.on("alert", function(msg) {\n  alert("Triggered " + msg);\n});\n\nobject.trigger("alert", "an event");\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    For example, to make a handy event dispatcher that can coordinate events\n      among different areas of your application:\n    <tt>\n     var dispatcher = _.clone(Backbone.Events)\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p id="Events-on">\n    <b class="header">\n     on\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.on(event, callback, [context])\n    </code>\n    <span class="alias">\n     Alias: bind\n    </span>\n    <br/>\n    Bind a\n    <b>\n     callback\n    </b>\n    function to an object. The callback will be invoked\n      whenever the\n    <b>\n     event\n    </b>\n    is fired.\n      If you have a large number of different events on a page, the convention is to use colons to\n      namespace them:\n    <tt>\n     "poll:start"\n    </tt>\n    , or\n    <tt>\n     "change:selection"\n    </tt>\n    .\n      The event string may also be a space-delimited list of several events...\n   </p>\n   <pre>book.on("change:title change:author", ...);\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    To supply a\n    <b>\n     context\n    </b>\n    value for\n    <tt>\n     this\n    </tt>\n    when the callback is invoked,\n      pass the optional third argument:\n    <tt>\n     model.on(\'change\', this.render, this)\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Callbacks bound to the special\n    <tt>\n     "all"\n    </tt>\n    event will be triggered when any event occurs, and are passed\n      the name of the event as the first argument. For example, to proxy all events\n      from one object to another:\n   </p>\n   <pre>proxy.on("all", function(eventName) {\n  object.trigger(eventName);\n});\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    All Backbone event methods also support an event map syntax, as an alternative\n      to positional arguments:\n   </p>\n   <pre>book.on({\n  "change:title": titleView.update,\n  "change:author": authorPane.update,\n  "destroy": bookView.remove\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Events-off">\n    <b class="header">\n     off\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.off([event], [callback], [context])\n    </code>\n    <span class="alias">\n     Alias: unbind\n    </span>\n    <br/>\n    Remove a previously-bound\n    <b>\n     callback\n    </b>\n    function from an object. If no\n    <b>\n     context\n    </b>\n    is specified, all of the versions of the callback with\n      different contexts will be removed. If no\n      callback is specified, all callbacks for the\n    <b>\n     event\n    </b>\n    will be\n      removed. If no event is specified, callbacks for\n    <i>\n     all\n    </i>\n    events\n      will be removed.\n   </p>\n   <pre>// Removes just the `onChange` callback.\nobject.off("change", onChange);\n\n// Removes all "change" callbacks.\nobject.off("change");\n\n// Removes the `onChange` callback for all events.\nobject.off(null, onChange);\n\n// Removes all callbacks for `context` for all events.\nobject.off(null, null, context);\n\n// Removes all callbacks on `object`.\nobject.off();\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    Note that calling\n    <tt>\n     model.off()\n    </tt>\n    , for example, will indeed remove\n    <i>\n     all\n    </i>\n    events\n      on the model \xe2\x80\x94 including events that Backbone uses for internal bookkeeping.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Events-trigger">\n    <b class="header">\n     trigger\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.trigger(event, [*args])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Trigger callbacks for the given\n    <b>\n     event\n    </b>\n    , or space-delimited list of events.\n      Subsequent arguments to\n    <b>\n     trigger\n    </b>\n    will be passed along to the\n      event callbacks.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Events-once">\n    <b class="header">\n     once\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.once(event, callback, [context])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Just like\n    <a href="#Events-on">\n     on\n    </a>\n    , but causes the bound callback to only\n      fire once before being removed. Handy for saying "the next time that X happens, do this".\n   </p>\n   <p id="Events-listenTo">\n    <b class="header">\n     listenTo\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.listenTo(other, event, callback)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Tell an\n    <b>\n     object\n    </b>\n    to listen to a particular event on an\n    <b>\n     other\n    </b>\n    object.  The advantage of using this form, instead of\n    <tt>\n     other.on(event,\n      callback, object)\n    </tt>\n    , is that\n    <b>\n     listenTo\n    </b>\n    allows the\n    <b>\n     object\n    </b>\n    to keep track of the events, and they can be removed all at once later\n      on.  The\n    <b>\n     callback\n    </b>\n    will always be called with\n    <b>\n     object\n    </b>\n    as\n      context.\n   </p>\n   <pre>view.listenTo(model, \'change\', view.render);\n</pre>\n   <p id="Events-stopListening">\n    <b class="header">\n     stopListening\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.stopListening([other], [event], [callback])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Tell an\n    <b>\n     object\n    </b>\n    to stop listening to events. Either call\n    <b>\n     stopListening\n    </b>\n    with no arguments to have the\n    <b>\n     object\n    </b>\n    remove\n      all of its\n    <a href="#Events-listenTo">\n     registered\n    </a>\n    callbacks ... or be more\n      precise by telling it to remove just the events it\'s listening to on a\n      specific object, or a specific event, or just a specific callback.\n   </p>\n   <pre>view.stopListening();\n\nview.stopListening(model);\n</pre>\n   <p id="Events-listenToOnce">\n    <b class="header">\n     listenToOnce\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.listenToOnce(other, event, callback)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Just like\n    <a href="#Events-listenTo">\n     listenTo\n    </a>\n    , but causes the bound\n      callback to only fire once before being removed.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Events-catalog">\n    <b class="header">\n     Catalog of Events\n    </b>\n    <br/>\n    Here\'s the complete list of built-in Backbone events, with arguments.\n      You\'re also free to trigger your own events on Models, Collections and\n      Views as you see fit. The\n    <tt>\n     Backbone\n    </tt>\n    object itself mixes in\n    <tt>\n     Events\n    </tt>\n    ,\n      and can be used to emit any global events that your application needs.\n   </p>\n   <ul class="small">\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "add"\n     </b>\n     (model, collection, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model is added to a collection.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "remove"\n     </b>\n     (model, collection, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model is removed from a collection.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "reset"\n     </b>\n     (collection, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when the collection\'s entire contents have been replaced.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "sort"\n     </b>\n     (collection, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when the collection has been re-sorted.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "change"\n     </b>\n     (model, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model\'s attributes have changed.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "change:[attribute]"\n     </b>\n     (model, value, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a specific attribute has been updated.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "destroy"\n     </b>\n     (model, collection, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model is\n     <a href="#Model-destroy">\n      destroyed\n     </a>\n     .\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "request"\n     </b>\n     (model_or_collection, xhr, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model or collection has started a request to the server.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "sync"\n     </b>\n     (model_or_collection, resp, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model or collection has been successfully synced with the server.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "error"\n     </b>\n     (model_or_collection, resp, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when model\'s or collection\'s request to remote server has failed.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "invalid"\n     </b>\n     (model, error, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model\'s\n     <a href="#Model-validate">\n      validation\n     </a>\n     fails on the client.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "route:[name]"\n     </b>\n     (params) \xe2\x80\x94 Fired by the router when a specific route is matched.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "route"\n     </b>\n     (route, params) \xe2\x80\x94 Fired by the router when\n     <i>\n      any\n     </i>\n     route has been matched.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "route"\n     </b>\n     (router, route, params) \xe2\x80\x94 Fired by history when\n     <i>\n      any\n     </i>\n     route has been matched.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "all"\n     </b>\n     \xe2\x80\x94 this special event fires for\n     <i>\n      any\n     </i>\n     triggered event, passing the event name as the first argument.\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   <p>\n    Generally speaking, when calling a function that emits an event\n      (\n    <tt>\n     model.set\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     collection.add\n    </tt>\n    , and so on...),\n      if you\'d like to prevent the event from being triggered, you may pass\n    <tt>\n     {silent: true}\n    </tt>\n    as an option. Note that this is\n    <i>\n     rarely\n    </i>\n    ,\n      perhaps even never, a good idea. Passing through a specific flag\n      in the options for your event callback to look at, and choose to ignore,\n      will usually work out better.\n   </p>\n   <h2 id="Model">\n    Backbone.Model\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     Models\n    </b>\n    are the heart of any JavaScript application, containing\n      the interactive data as well as a large part of the logic surrounding it:\n      conversions, validations, computed properties, and access control. You\n      extend\n    <b>\n     Backbone.Model\n    </b>\n    with your domain-specific methods, and\n    <b>\n     Model\n    </b>\n    provides a basic set of functionality for managing changes.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The following is a contrived example, but it demonstrates defining a model\n      with a custom method, setting an attribute, and firing an event keyed\n      to changes in that specific attribute.\n      After running this code once,\n    <tt>\n     sidebar\n    </tt>\n    will be\n      available in your browser\'s console, so you can play around with it.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var Sidebar = Backbone.Model.extend({\n  promptColor: function() {\n    var cssColor = prompt("Please enter a CSS color:");\n    this.set({color: cssColor});\n  }\n});\n\nwindow.sidebar = new Sidebar;\n\nsidebar.on(\'change:color\', function(model, color) {\n  $(\'#sidebar\').css({background: color});\n});\n\nsidebar.set({color: \'white\'});\n\nsidebar.promptColor();\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-extend">\n    <b class="header">\n     extend\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     Backbone.Model.extend(properties, [classProperties])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    To create a\n    <b>\n     Model\n    </b>\n    class of your own, you extend\n    <b>\n     Backbone.Model\n    </b>\n    and provide instance\n    <b>\n     properties\n    </b>\n    , as well as optional\n    <b>\n     classProperties\n    </b>\n    to be attached directly to the constructor function.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     extend\n    </b>\n    correctly sets up the prototype chain, so subclasses created\n      with\n    <b>\n     extend\n    </b>\n    can be further extended and subclassed as far as you like.\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Note = Backbone.Model.extend({\n\n  initialize: function() { ... },\n\n  author: function() { ... },\n\n  coordinates: function() { ... },\n\n  allowedToEdit: function(account) {\n    return true;\n  }\n\n});\n\nvar PrivateNote = Note.extend({\n\n  allowedToEdit: function(account) {\n    return account.owns(this);\n  }\n\n});\n</pre>\n   <p class="warning">\n    Brief aside on\n    <tt>\n     super\n    </tt>\n    : JavaScript does not provide\n        a simple way to call super \xe2\x80\x94 the function of the same name defined\n        higher on the prototype chain. If you override a core function like\n    <tt>\n     set\n    </tt>\n    , or\n    <tt>\n     save\n    </tt>\n    , and you want to invoke the\n        parent object\'s implementation, you\'ll have to explicitly call it, along these lines:\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Note = Backbone.Model.extend({\n  set: function(attributes, options) {\n    Backbone.Model.prototype.set.apply(this, arguments);\n    ...\n  }\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-constructor">\n    <b class="header">\n     constructor / initialize\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     new Model([attributes], [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    When creating an instance of a model, you can pass in the initial values\n      of the\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    , which will be\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    on the\n      model. If you define an\n    <b>\n     initialize\n    </b>\n    function, it will be invoked when\n      the model is created.\n   </p>\n   <pre>new Book({\n  title: "One Thousand and One Nights",\n  author: "Scheherazade"\n});\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    In rare cases, if you\'re looking to get fancy,\n      you may want to override\n    <b>\n     constructor\n    </b>\n    , which allows\n      you to replace the actual constructor function for your model.\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Library = Backbone.Model.extend({\n  constructor: function() {\n    this.books = new Books();\n    Backbone.Model.apply(this, arguments);\n  },\n  parse: function(data, options) {\n    this.books.reset(data.books);\n    return data.library;\n  }\n});\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    If you pass a\n    <tt>\n     {collection: ...}\n    </tt>\n    as the\n    <b>\n     options\n    </b>\n    , the model\n      gains a\n    <tt>\n     collection\n    </tt>\n    property that will be used to indicate which\n      collection the model belongs to, and is used to help compute the model\'s\n    <a href="#Model-url">\n     url\n    </a>\n    . The\n    <tt>\n     model.collection\n    </tt>\n    property is\n      normally created automatically when you first add a model to a collection.\n      Note that the reverse is not true, as passing this option to the constructor\n      will not automatically add the model to the collection. Useful, sometimes.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    If\n    <tt>\n     {parse: true}\n    </tt>\n    is passed as an\n    <b>\n     option\n    </b>\n    , the\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    will first be converted by\n    <a href="#Model-parse">\n     parse\n    </a>\n    before being\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    on the model.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-get">\n    <b class="header">\n     get\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.get(attribute)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Get the current value of an attribute from the model. For example:\n    <tt>\n     note.get("title")\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-set">\n    <b class="header">\n     set\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.set(attributes, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Set a hash of attributes (one or many) on the model. If any of the attributes\n      change the model\'s state, a\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event will be triggered on the model.\n      Change events for specific attributes are also triggered, and you can bind\n      to those as well, for example:\n    <tt>\n     change:title\n    </tt>\n    , and\n    <tt>\n     change:content\n    </tt>\n    .\n      You may also pass individual keys and values.\n   </p>\n   <pre>note.set({title: "March 20", content: "In his eyes she eclipses..."});\n\nbook.set("title", "A Scandal in Bohemia");\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-escape">\n    <b class="header">\n     escape\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.escape(attribute)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Similar to\n    <a href="#Model-get">\n     get\n    </a>\n    , but returns the HTML-escaped version\n      of a model\'s attribute. If you\'re interpolating data from the model into\n      HTML, using\n    <b>\n     escape\n    </b>\n    to retrieve attributes will prevent\n    <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cross-site_scripting">\n     XSS\n    </a>\n    attacks.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var hacker = new Backbone.Model({\n  name: "&lt;script&gt;alert(\'xss\')&lt;/script&gt;"\n});\n\nalert(hacker.escape(\'name\'));\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-has">\n    <b class="header">\n     has\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.has(attribute)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Returns\n    <tt>\n     true\n    </tt>\n    if the attribute is set to a non-null or non-undefined\n      value.\n   </p>\n   <pre>if (note.has("title")) {\n  ...\n}\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-unset">\n    <b class="header">\n     unset\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.unset(attribute, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Remove an attribute by deleting it from the internal attributes hash.\n      Fires a\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event unless\n    <tt>\n     silent\n    </tt>\n    is passed as an option.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-clear">\n    <b class="header">\n     clear\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.clear([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Removes all attributes from the model, including the\n    <tt>\n     id\n    </tt>\n    attribute. Fires a\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event unless\n    <tt>\n     silent\n    </tt>\n    is passed as an option.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-id">\n    <b class="header">\n     id\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.id\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    A special property of models, the\n    <b>\n     id\n    </b>\n    is an arbitrary string\n      (integer id or UUID). If you set the\n    <b>\n     id\n    </b>\n    in the\n      attributes hash, it will be copied onto the model as a direct property.\n      Models can be retrieved by id from collections, and the id is used to generate\n      model URLs by default.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-idAttribute">\n    <b class="header">\n     idAttribute\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.idAttribute\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    A model\'s unique identifier is stored under the\n    <tt>\n     id\n    </tt>\n    attribute.\n      If you\'re directly communicating with a backend (CouchDB, MongoDB) that uses\n      a different unique key, you may set a Model\'s\n    <tt>\n     idAttribute\n    </tt>\n    to\n      transparently map from that key to\n    <tt>\n     id\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var Meal = Backbone.Model.extend({\n  idAttribute: "_id"\n});\n\nvar cake = new Meal({ _id: 1, name: "Cake" });\nalert("Cake id: " + cake.id);\n</pre>\n   <p>\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-cid">\n    <b class="header">\n     cid\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.cid\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    A special property of models, the\n    <b>\n     cid\n    </b>\n    or client id is a unique identifier\n      automatically assigned to all models when they\'re first created. Client ids\n      are handy when the model has not yet been saved to the server, and does not\n      yet have its eventual true\n    <b>\n     id\n    </b>\n    , but already needs to be visible in the UI.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-attributes">\n    <b class="header">\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.attributes\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    The\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    property is the internal hash containing the model\'s\n      state \xe2\x80\x94 usually (but not necessarily) a form of the JSON object\n      representing the model data on the server. It\'s often a straightforward\n      serialization of a row from the database, but it could also be client-side\n      computed state.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Please use\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    to update the\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    instead of modifying them directly. If you\'d like to retrieve and munge a\n      copy of the model\'s attributes, use\n    <tt>\n     _.clone(model.attributes)\n    </tt>\n    instead.\n   </p>\n   <p class="warning">\n    Due to the fact that\n    <a href="#Events">\n     Events\n    </a>\n    accepts space separated\n      lists of events, attribute names should not include spaces.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-changed">\n    <b class="header">\n     changed\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.changed\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    The\n    <b>\n     changed\n    </b>\n    property is the internal hash containing all the attributes\n      that have changed since the last\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    .\n      Please do not update\n    <b>\n     changed\n    </b>\n    directly since its state is internally maintained\n      by\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    .  A copy of\n    <b>\n     changed\n    </b>\n    can be acquired from\n    <a href="#Model-changedAttributes">\n     changedAttributes\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-defaults">\n    <b class="header">\n     defaults\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.defaults or model.defaults()\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    The\n    <b>\n     defaults\n    </b>\n    hash (or function) can be used to specify the default\n      attributes for your model. When creating an instance of the model,\n      any unspecified attributes will be set to their default value.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var Meal = Backbone.Model.extend({\n  defaults: {\n    "appetizer":  "caesar salad",\n    "entree":     "ravioli",\n    "dessert":    "cheesecake"\n  }\n});\n\nalert("Dessert will be " + (new Meal).get(\'dessert\'));\n</pre>\n   <p class="warning">\n    Remember that in JavaScript, objects are passed by reference, so if you\n      include an object as a default value, it will be shared among all instances.\n      Instead, define\n    <b>\n     defaults\n    </b>\n    as a function.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-toJSON">\n    <b class="header">\n     toJSON\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.toJSON([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Return a shallow copy of the model\'s\n    <a href="#Model-attributes">\n     attributes\n    </a>\n    for JSON stringification.  This can be used for persistence,\n      serialization, or for augmentation before being sent to the server. The\n      name of this method is a bit confusing, as it doesn\'t actually return a\n      JSON string \xe2\x80\x94 but I\'m afraid that it\'s the way that the\n    <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/JSON#toJSON()_method">\n     JavaScript API for\n     <b>\n      JSON.stringify\n     </b>\n    </a>\n    works.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var artist = new Backbone.Model({\n  firstName: "Wassily",\n  lastName: "Kandinsky"\n});\n\nartist.set({birthday: "December 16, 1866"});\n\nalert(JSON.stringify(artist));\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-sync">\n    <b class="header">\n     sync\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.sync(method, model, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Uses\n    <a href="#Sync">\n     Backbone.sync\n    </a>\n    to persist the state of a model to\n      the server.  Can be overridden for custom behavior.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-fetch">\n    <b class="header">\n     fetch\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.fetch([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Resets the model\'s state from the server by delegating to\n    <a href="#Sync">\n     Backbone.sync\n    </a>\n    . Returns a\n    <a href="http://api.jquery.com/jQuery.ajax/#jqXHR">\n     jqXHR\n    </a>\n    .\n      Useful if the model has never\n      been populated with data, or if you\'d like to ensure that you have the\n      latest server state. A\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event will be triggered if the\n      server\'s state differs from the current attributes. Accepts\n    <tt>\n     success\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     error\n    </tt>\n    callbacks in the options hash, which\n      are both passed\n    <tt>\n     (model, response, options)\n    </tt>\n    as arguments.\n   </p>\n   <pre>// Poll every 10 seconds to keep the channel model up-to-date.\nsetInterval(function() {\n  channel.fetch();\n}, 10000);\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-save">\n    <b class="header">\n     save\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.save([attributes], [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Save a model to your database (or alternative persistence layer),\n      by delegating to\n    <a href="#Sync">\n     Backbone.sync\n    </a>\n    .  Returns a\n    <a href="http://api.jquery.com/jQuery.ajax/#jqXHR">\n     jqXHR\n    </a>\n    if\n      validation is successful and\n    <tt>\n     false\n    </tt>\n    otherwise. The\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    hash (as in\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    ) should contain the attributes\n      you\'d like to change \xe2\x80\x94 keys that aren\'t mentioned won\'t be altered \xe2\x80\x94 but,\n      a\n    <i>\n     complete representation\n    </i>\n    of the resource will be sent to the server.\n      As with\n    <tt>\n     set\n    </tt>\n    , you may pass individual keys and values instead of a hash.\n      If the model has a\n    <a href="#Model-validate">\n     validate\n    </a>\n    method, and validation fails, the model will not be saved. If the model\n    <a href="#Model-isNew">\n     isNew\n    </a>\n    , the save will be a\n    <tt>\n     "create"\n    </tt>\n    (HTTP\n    <tt>\n     POST\n    </tt>\n    ), if the model already\n      exists on the server, the save will be an\n    <tt>\n     "update"\n    </tt>\n    (HTTP\n    <tt>\n     PUT\n    </tt>\n    ).\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    If instead, you\'d only like the\n    <i>\n     changed\n    </i>\n    attributes to be sent to the\n      server, call\n    <tt>\n     model.save(attrs, {patch: true})\n    </tt>\n    . You\'ll get an HTTP\n    <tt>\n     PATCH\n    </tt>\n    request to the server with just the passed-in attributes.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Calling\n    <tt>\n     save\n    </tt>\n    with new attributes will cause a\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event immediately, a\n    <tt>\n     "request"\n    </tt>\n    event as the Ajax request begins to\n      go to the server, and a\n    <tt>\n     "sync"\n    </tt>\n    event after the server has acknowledged\n      the successful change. Pass\n    <tt>\n     {wait: true}\n    </tt>\n    if you\'d like to wait\n      for the server before setting the new attributes on the model.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    In the following example, notice how our overridden version\n      of\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.sync\n    </tt>\n    receives a\n    <tt>\n     "create"\n    </tt>\n    request\n      the first time the model is saved and an\n    <tt>\n     "update"\n    </tt>\n    request the second time.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">Backbone.sync = function(method, model) {\n  alert(method + ": " + JSON.stringify(model));\n  model.set(\'id\', 1);\n};\n\nvar book = new Backbone.Model({\n  title: "The Rough Riders",\n  author: "Theodore Roosevelt"\n});\n\nbook.save();\n\nbook.save({author: "Teddy"});\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     save\n    </b>\n    accepts\n    <tt>\n     success\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     error\n    </tt>\n    callbacks in the\n      options hash, which will be passed the arguments\n    <tt>\n     (model, response, options)\n    </tt>\n    .\n      If a server-side validation fails, return a non-\n    <tt>\n     200\n    </tt>\n    HTTP response code, along with an error response in text or JSON.\n   </p>\n   <pre>book.save("author", "F.D.R.", {error: function(){ ... }});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-destroy">\n    <b class="header">\n     destroy\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.destroy([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Destroys the model on the server by delegating an HTTP\n    <tt>\n     DELETE\n    </tt>\n    request to\n    <a href="#Sync">\n     Backbone.sync\n    </a>\n    . Returns a\n    <a href="http://api.jquery.com/jQuery.ajax/#jqXHR">\n     jqXHR\n    </a>\n    object, or\n    <tt>\n     false\n    </tt>\n    if the model\n    <a href="#Model-isNew">\n     isNew\n    </a>\n    . Accepts\n    <tt>\n     success\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     error\n    </tt>\n    callbacks in the options hash, which\n      will be passed\n    <tt>\n     (model, response, options)\n    </tt>\n    .\n      Triggers a\n    <tt>\n     "destroy"\n    </tt>\n    event on the model, which will bubble up\n      through any collections that contain it, a\n    <tt>\n     "request"\n    </tt>\n    event as it\n      begins the Ajax request to the server, and a\n    <tt>\n     "sync"\n    </tt>\n    event, after\n      the server has successfully acknowledged the model\'s deletion. By default\n    <b>\n     validate\n    </b>\n    is called before\n    <tt>\n     save\n    </tt>\n    , but can also be called before\n    <tt>\n     set\n    </tt>\n    if\n    <tt>\n     {validate:true}\n    </tt>\n    is passed. You can bind\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    events\n      to be notified when any model in the collection has been modified,\n      listen for\n    <tt>\n     "add"\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     "remove"\n    </tt>\n    events,\n    <tt>\n     fetch\n    </tt>\n    the collection from the server, and use a full suite of\n    <a href="#Collection-Underscore-Methods">\n     Underscore.js methods\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Any event that is triggered on a model in a collection will also be\n      triggered on the collection directly, for convenience.\n      This allows you to listen for changes to specific attributes in any\n      model in a collection, for example:\n    <tt>\n     documents.on("change:selected", ...)\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-extend">\n    <b class="header">\n     extend\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     Backbone.Collection.extend(properties, [classProperties])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    To create a\n    <b>\n     Collection\n    </b>\n    class of your own, extend\n    <b>\n     Backbone.Collection\n    </b>\n    ,\n      providing instance\n    <b>\n     properties\n    </b>\n    , as well as optional\n    <b>\n     classProperties\n    </b>\n    to be attached\n      directly to the collection\'s constructor function.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-model">\n    <b class="header">\n     model\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.model\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Override this property to specify the model class that the collection\n      contains. Use\n    <b>\n     reset\n    </b>\n    to replace a collection with a new list\n      of models (or attribute hashes), triggering a single\n    <tt>\n     "reset"\n    </tt>\n    event\n      at the end. Returns the newly-set models.\n      For convenience, within a\n    <tt>\n     "reset"\n    </tt>\n    event, the list of any\n      previous models is available as\n    <tt>\n     options.previousModels\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Here\'s an example using\n    <b>\n     reset\n    </b>\n    to bootstrap a collection during initial page load,\n      in a Rails application:\n   </p>\n   <pre>&lt;script&gt;\n  var accounts = new Backbone.Collection;\n  accounts.reset(&lt;%= @accounts.to_json %&gt;);\n&lt;/script&gt;\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    Calling\n    <tt>\n     collection.reset()\n    </tt>\n    without passing any models as arguments\n      will empty the entire collection.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-set">\n    <b class="header">\n     set\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.set(models, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    The\n    <b>\n     set\n    </b>\n    method performs a "smart" update of the collection\n      with the passed list of models. If a model in the list isn\'t yet in the\n      collection it will be added; if the model is already in the collection\n      its attributes will be merged; and if the collection contains any models that\n    <i>\n     aren\'t\n    </i>\n    present in the list, they\'ll be removed. All of the appropriate\n    <tt>\n     "add"\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     "remove"\n    </tt>\n    , and\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    events are fired\n      as this happens. Returns the touched models in the collection.\n      If you\'d like to customize the behavior, you can disable\n      it with options:\n    <tt>\n     {add: false}\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     {remove: false}\n    </tt>\n    , or\n    <tt>\n     {merge: false}\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <pre>var vanHalen = new Backbone.Collection([eddie, alex, stone, roth]);\n\nvanHalen.set([eddie, alex, stone, hagar]);\n\n// Fires a "remove" event for roth, and an "add" event for "hagar".\n// Updates any of stone, alex, and eddie\'s attributes that may have\n// changed over the years.\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-get">\n    <b class="header">\n     get\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.get(id)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Get a model from a collection, specified by an\n    <a href="#Model-id">\n     id\n    </a>\n    ,\n      a\n    <a href="#Model-cid">\n     cid\n    </a>\n    , or by passing in a\n    <b>\n     model\n    </b>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <pre>var book = library.get(110);\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-at">\n    <b class="header">\n     at\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.at(index)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Get a model from a collection, specified by index. Useful if your collection\n      is sorted, and if your collection isn\'t sorted,\n    <b>\n     at\n    </b>\n    will still\n      retrieve models in insertion order.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-push">\n    <b class="header">\n     push\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.push(model, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Add a model at the end of a collection. Takes the same options as\n    <a href="#Collection-add">\n     add\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-pop">\n    <b class="header">\n     pop\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.pop([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Remove and return the last model from a collection. Takes the same options as\n    <a href="#Collection-remove">\n     remove\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-unshift">\n    <b class="header">\n     unshift\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.unshift(model, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Add a model at the beginning of a collection. Takes the same options as\n    <a href="#Collection-add">\n     add\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-shift">\n    <b class="header">\n     shift\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.shift([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Remove and return the first model from a collection. Takes the same options as\n    <a href="#Collection-remove">\n     remove\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-slice">\n    <b class="header">\n     slice\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.slice(begin, end)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Return a shallow copy of this collection\'s models, using the same options as\n      native\n    <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/slice">\n     Array#slice\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-length">\n    <b class="header">\n     length\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.length\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Like an array, a Collection maintains a\n    <tt>\n     length\n    </tt>\n    property, counting\n      the number of models it contains.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-comparator">\n    <b class="header">\n     comparator\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.comparator\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    By default there is no\n    <b>\n     comparator\n    </b>\n    for a collection.\n      If you define a comparator, it will be used to maintain\n      the collection in sorted order. This means that as models are added,\n      they are inserted at the correct index in\n    <tt>\n     collection.models\n    </tt>\n    .\n      A comparator can be defined as a\n    <a href="http://underscorejs.org/#sortBy">\n     sortBy\n    </a>\n    (pass a function that takes a single argument),\n      as a\n    <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/sort">\n     sort\n    </a>\n    (pass a comparator function that expects two arguments),\n      or as a string indicating the attribute to sort by.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    "sortBy" comparator functions take a model and return a numeric or string\n      value by which the model should be ordered relative to others.\n      "sort" comparator functions take two models, and return\n    <tt>\n     -1\n    </tt>\n    if\n      the first model should come before the second,\n    <tt>\n     0\n    </tt>\n    if they are of\n      the same rank and\n    <tt>\n     1\n    </tt>\n    if the first model should come after.\n    <i>\n     Note that Backbone depends on the arity of your comparator function to\n      determine between the two styles, so be careful if your comparator function\n      is bound.\n    </i>\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Note how even though all of the chapters in this example are added backwards,\n      they come out in the proper order:\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var Chapter  = Backbone.Model;\nvar chapters = new Backbone.Collection;\n\nchapters.comparator = \'page\';\n\nchapters.add(new Chapter({page: 9, title: "The End"}));\nchapters.add(new Chapter({page: 5, title: "The Middle"}));\nchapters.add(new Chapter({page: 1, title: "The Beginning"}));\n\nalert(chapters.pluck(\'title\'));\n</pre>\n   <p class="warning">\n    Collections with a comparator will not automatically re-sort if you\n      later change model attributes, so you may wish to call\n    <tt>\n     sort\n    </tt>\n    after changing model attributes that would affect the order.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-sort">\n    <b class="header">\n     sort\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.sort([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Force a collection to re-sort itself. You don\'t need to call this under\n      normal circumstances, as a collection with a\n    <a href="#Collection-comparator">\n     comparator\n    </a>\n    will sort itself whenever a model is added. To disable sorting when adding\n      a model, pass\n    <tt>\n     {sort: false}\n    </tt>\n    to\n    <tt>\n     add\n    </tt>\n    . Calling\n    <b>\n     sort\n    </b>\n    triggers a\n    <tt>\n     "sort"\n    </tt>\n    event on the collection.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-pluck">\n    <b class="header">\n     pluck\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.pluck(attribute)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Pluck an attribute from each model in the collection. Equivalent to calling\n    <tt>\n     map\n    </tt>\n    and returning a single attribute from the iterator.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var stooges = new Backbone.Collection([\n  {name: "Curly"},\n  {name: "Larry"},\n  {name: "Moe"}\n]);\n\nvar names = stooges.pluck("name");\n\nalert(JSON.stringify(names));\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-where">\n    <b class="header">\n     where\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.where(attributes)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Return an array of all the models in a collection that match the\n      passed\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    . Useful for simple cases of\n    <tt>\n     filter\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var friends = new Backbone.Collection([\n  {name: "Athos",      job: "Musketeer"},\n  {name: "Porthos",    job: "Musketeer"},\n  {name: "Aramis",     job: "Musketeer"},\n  {name: "d\'Artagnan", job: "Guard"},\n]);\n\nvar musketeers = friends.where({job: "Musketeer"});\n\nalert(musketeers.length);\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-findWhere">\n    <b class="header">\n     findWhere\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.findWhere(attributes)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Just like\n    <a href="#Collection-where">\n     where\n    </a>\n    , but directly returns only\n      the first model in the collection that matches the passed\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-url">\n    <b class="header">\n     url\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.url or collection.url()\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Set the\n    <b>\n     url\n    </b>\n    property (or function) on a collection to reference\n      its location on the server. Models within the collection will use\n    <b>\n     url\n    </b>\n    to construct URLs of their own.\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Notes = Backbone.Collection.extend({\n  url: \'/notes\'\n});\n\n// Or, something more sophisticated:\n\nvar Notes = Backbone.Collection.extend({\n  url: function() {\n    return this.document.url() + \'/notes\';\n  }\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-parse">\n    <b class="header">\n     parse\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.parse(response, options)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    <b>\n     parse\n    </b>\n    is called by Backbone whenever a collection\'s models are\n      returned by the server, in\n    <a href="#Collection-fetch">\n     fetch\n    </a>\n    .\n      The function is passed the raw\n    <tt>\n     response\n    </tt>\n    object, and should return\n      the array of model attributes to be\n    <a href="#Collection-add">\n     added\n    </a>\n    to the collection. The default implementation is a no-op, simply passing\n      through the JSON response. Override this if you need to work with a\n      preexisting API, or better namespace your responses.\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Tweets = Backbone.Collection.extend({\n  // The Twitter Search API returns tweets under "results".\n  parse: function(response) {\n    return response.results;\n  }\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-clone">\n    <b class="header">\n     clone\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.clone()\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Returns a new instance of the collection with an identical list of models.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-fetch">\n    <b class="header">\n     fetch\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.fetch([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Fetch the default set of models for this collection from the server,\n    <a href="#Collection-set">\n     setting\n    </a>\n    them on the collection when they arrive.\n      The\n    <b>\n     options\n    </b>\n    hash takes\n    <tt>\n     success\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     error\n    </tt>\n    callbacks\n      which will both be passed\n    <tt>\n     (collection, response, options)\n    </tt>\n    as arguments.\n      When the model data returns from the server, it uses\n    <a href="#Collection-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    to (intelligently) merge the fetched models, unless you pass\n    <tt>\n     {reset: true}\n    </tt>\n    ,\n      in which case the collection will be (efficiently)\n    <a href="#Collection-reset">\n     reset\n    </a>\n    .\n      Delegates to\n    <a href="#Sync">\n     Backbone.sync\n    </a>\n    under the covers for custom persistence strategies and returns a\n    <a href="http://api.jquery.com/jQuery.ajax/#jqXHR">\n     jqXHR\n    </a>\n    .\n      The server handler for\n    <b>\n     fetch\n    </b>\n    requests should return a JSON array of\n      models.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">Backbone.sync = function(method, model) {\n  alert(method + ": " + model.url);\n};\n\nvar accounts = new Backbone.Collection;\naccounts.url = \'/accounts\';\n\naccounts.fetch();\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    The behavior of\n    <b>\n     fetch\n    </b>\n    can be customized by using the available\n    <a href="#Collection-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    options. For example, to fetch a\n      collection, getting an\n    <tt>\n     "add"\n    </tt>\n    event for every new model, and\n      a\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event for every changed existing model, without\n      removing anything:\n    <tt>\n     collection.fetch({remove: false})\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     jQuery.ajax\n    </b>\n    options can also be passed directly as\n    <b>\n     fetch\n    </b>\n    options,\n      so to fetch a specific page of a paginated collection:\n    <tt>\n     Documents.fetch({data: {page: 3}})\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Note that\n    <b>\n     fetch\n    </b>\n    should not be used to populate collections on\n      page load \xe2\x80\x94 all models needed at load time should already be\n    <a href="#FAQ-bootstrap">\n     bootstrapped\n    </a>\n    in to place.\n    <b>\n     fetch\n    </b>\n    is\n      intended for lazily-loading models for interfaces that are not needed\n      immediately: for example, documents with collections of notes that may be\n      toggled open and closed.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-create">\n    <b class="header">\n     create\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.create(attributes, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Convenience to create a new instance of a model within a collection.\n      Equivalent to instantiating a model with a hash of attributes,\n      saving the model to the server, and adding the model to the set after being\n      successfully created. Returns the new model. If client-side validation\n      failed, the model will be unsaved, with validation errors.\n      In order for this to work, you should set the\n    <a href="#Collection-model">\n     model\n    </a>\n    property of the collection.\n      The\n    <b>\n     create\n    </b>\n    method can accept either an attributes hash or an\n      existing, unsaved model object.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Creating a model will cause an immediate\n    <tt>\n     "add"\n    </tt>\n    event to be\n      triggered on the collection, a\n    <tt>\n     "request"\n    </tt>\n    event as the new model is\n      sent to the server, as well as a\n    <tt>\n     "sync"\n    </tt>\n    event, once the\n      server has responded with the successful creation of the model. Pass\n    <tt>\n     {wait: true}\n    </tt>\n    if you\'d like to wait for the server before adding the new model to the collection.\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Library = Backbone.Collection.extend({\n  model: Book\n});\n\nvar nypl = new Library;\n\nvar othello = nypl.create({\n  title: "Othello",\n  author: "William Shakespeare"\n});\n</pre>\n   <h2 id="Router">\n    Backbone.Router\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    Web applications often provide linkable, bookmarkable, shareable URLs for\n      important locations in the app. Until recently, hash fragments\n      (\n    <tt>\n     #page\n    </tt>\n    ) were used to provide these permalinks, but with the\n      arrival of the History API, it\'s now possible to use standard URLs (\n    <tt>\n     /page\n    </tt>\n    ).\n    <b>\n     Backbone.Router\n    </b>\n    provides methods for routing client-side pages, and\n      connecting them to actions and events. For browsers which don\'t yet support\n      the History API, the Router handles graceful fallback and transparent\n      translation to the fragment version of the URL.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    During page load, after your application has finished creating all of its routers,\n      be sure to call\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.history.start()\n    </tt>\n    , or\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.history.start({pushState: true})\n    </tt>\n    to route the initial URL.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Router-extend">\n    <b class="header">\n     extend\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     Backbone.Router.extend(properties, [classProperties])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Get started by creating a custom router class. Define actions that are\n      triggered when certain URL fragments are\n      matched, and provide a\n    <a href="#Router-routes">\n     routes\n    </a>\n    hash\n      that pairs routes to actions. Note that you\'ll want to avoid using a\n      leading slash in your route definitions:\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Workspace = Backbone.Router.extend({\n\n  routes: {\n    "help":                 "help",    // #help\n    "search/:query":        "search",  // #search/kiwis\n    "search/:query/p:page": "search"   // #search/kiwis/p7\n  },\n\n  help: function() {\n    ...\n  },\n\n  search: function(query, page) {\n    ...\n  }\n\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Router-routes">\n    <b class="header">\n     routes\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     router.routes\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    The routes hash maps URLs with parameters to functions on your router\n      (or just direct function definitions, if you prefer),\n      similar to the\n    <a href="#View">\n     View\n    </a>\n    \'s\n    <a href="#View-delegateEvents">\n     events hash\n    </a>\n    .\n      Routes can contain parameter parts,\n    <tt>\n     :param\n    </tt>\n    , which match a single URL\n      component between slashes; and splat parts\n    <tt>\n     *splat\n    </tt>\n    , which can match\n      any number of URL components. Part of a route can be made optional by\n      surrounding it in parentheses\n    <tt>\n     (/:optional)\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    For example, a route of\n    <tt>\n     "search/:query/p:page"\n    </tt>\n    will match\n      a fragment of\n    <tt>\n     #search/obama/p2\n    </tt>\n    , passing\n    <tt>\n     "obama"\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     "2"\n    </tt>\n    to the action.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    A route of\n    <tt>\n     "file/*path"\n    </tt>\n    will match\n    <tt>\n     #file/nested/folder/file.txt\n    </tt>\n    , passing\n    <tt>\n     "nested/folder/file.txt"\n    </tt>\n    to the action.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    A route of\n    <tt>\n     "docs/:section(/:subsection)"\n    </tt>\n    will match\n    <tt>\n     #docs/faq\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     #docs/faq/installing\n    </tt>\n    , passing\n    <tt>\n     "faq"\n    </tt>\n    to the action in the first case, and passing\n    <tt>\n     "faq"\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     "installing"\n    </tt>\n    to the action in the second.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Trailing slashes are treated as part of the URL, and (correctly) treated\n      as a unique route when accessed.\n    <tt>\n     docs\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     docs/\n    </tt>\n    will fire\n      different callbacks. If you can\'t avoid generating both types of URLs, you\n      can define a\n    <tt>\n     "docs(/)"\n    </tt>\n    matcher to capture both cases.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    When the visitor presses the back button, or enters a URL, and a particular\n      route is matched, the name of the action will be fired as an\n    <a href="#Events">\n     event\n    </a>\n    , so that other objects can listen to the router,\n      and be notified. In the following example, visiting\n    <tt>\n     #help/uploading\n    </tt>\n    will fire a\n    <tt>\n     route:help\n    </tt>\n    event from the router.\n   </p>\n   <pre>routes: {\n  "help/:page":         "help",\n  "download/*path":     "download",\n  "folder/:name":       "openFolder",\n  "folder/:name-:mode": "openFolder"\n}\n</pre>\n   <pre>router.on("route:help", function(page) {\n  ...\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Router-constructor">\n    <b class="header">\n     constructor / initialize\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     new Router([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    When creating a new router, you may pass its\n    <a href="#Router-routes">\n     routes\n    </a>\n    hash directly as an option, if you\n      choose. All\n    <tt>\n     options\n    </tt>\n    will also be passed to your\n    <tt>\n     initialize\n    </tt>\n    function, if defined.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Router-route">\n    <b class="header">\n     route\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     router.route(route, name, [callback])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Manually create a route for the router, The\n    <tt>\n     route\n    </tt>\n    argument may\n      be a\n    <a href="#Router-routes">\n     routing string\n    </a>\n    or regular expression.\n      Each matching capture from the route or regular expression will be passed as\n      an argument to the callback. The\n    <tt>\n     name\n    </tt>\n    argument will be triggered as\n      a\n    <tt>\n     "route:name"\n    </tt>\n    event whenever the route is matched.  If the\n    <tt>\n     callback\n    </tt>\n    argument is omitted\n    <tt>\n     router[name]\n    </tt>\n    will be used\n      instead. Routes added later may override previously declared routes.\n   </p>\n   <pre>initialize: function(options) {\n\n  // Matches #page/10, passing "10"\n  this.route("page/:number", "page", function(number){ ... });\n\n  // Matches /117-a/b/c/open, passing "117-a/b/c" to this.open\n  this.route(/^(.*?)\\/open$/, "open");\n\n},\n\nopen: function(id) { ... }\n</pre>\n   <p id="Router-navigate">\n    <b class="header">\n     navigate\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     router.navigate(fragment, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Whenever you reach a point in your application that you\'d like to save\n      as a URL, call\n    <b>\n     navigate\n    </b>\n    in order to update the URL.\n      If you wish to also call the route function, set the\n    <b>\n     trigger\n    </b>\n    option to\n    <tt>\n     true\n    </tt>\n    .\n      To update the URL without creating an entry in the browser\'s history,\n      set the\n    <b>\n     replace\n    </b>\n    option to\n    <tt>\n     true\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <pre>openPage: function(pageNumber) {\n  this.document.pages.at(pageNumber).open();\n  this.navigate("page/" + pageNumber);\n}\n\n# Or ...\n\napp.navigate("help/troubleshooting", {trigger: true});\n\n# Or ...\n\napp.navigate("help/troubleshooting", {trigger: true, replace: true});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Router-execute">\n    <b class="header">\n     execute\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     router.execute(callback, args)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    This method is called internally within the router, whenever a route \n      matches and its corresponding\n    <b>\n     callback\n    </b>\n    is about to be executed. \n      Override it to perform custom parsing or wrapping of your routes, for \n      example, to parse query strings before handing them to your route\n      callback, like so:\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Router = Backbone.Router.extend({\n  execute: function(callback, args) {\n    args.push(parseQueryString(args.pop()));\n    if (callback) callback.apply(this, args);\n  }\n});\n</pre>\n   <h2 id="History">\n    Backbone.history\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     History\n    </b>\n    serves as a global router (per frame) to handle\n    <tt>\n     hashchange\n    </tt>\n    events or\n    <tt>\n     pushState\n    </tt>\n    , match the appropriate route, and trigger callbacks.\n      You shouldn\'t ever have to create one of these yourself since\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.history\n    </tt>\n    already contains one.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     pushState\n    </b>\n    support exists on a purely opt-in basis in Backbone.\n      Older browsers that don\'t support\n    <tt>\n     pushState\n    </tt>\n    will continue to use\n      hash-based URL fragments, and if a hash URL is visited by a\n    <tt>\n     pushState\n    </tt>\n    -capable browser, it will be transparently upgraded to\n      the true URL. Note that using real URLs requires your web server to be\n      able to correctly render those pages, so back-end changes are required\n      as well. For example, if you have a route of\n    <tt>\n     /documents/100\n    </tt>\n    ,\n      your web server must be able to serve that page, if the browser\n      visits that URL directly. For full search-engine crawlability, it\'s best to\n      have the server generate the complete HTML for the page ... but if it\'s a web\n      application, just rendering the same content you would have for the root URL,\n      and filling in the rest with Backbone Views and JavaScript works fine.\n   </p>\n   <p id="History-start">\n    <b class="header">\n     start\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     Backbone.history.start([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    When all of your\n    <a href="#Router">\n     Routers\n    </a>\n    have been created,\n      and all of the routes are set up properly, call\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.history.start()\n    </tt>\n    to begin monitoring\n    <tt>\n     hashchange\n    </tt>\n    events, and dispatching routes.\n      Subsequent calls to\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.history.start()\n    </tt>\n    will throw an error,\n      and\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.History.started\n    </tt>\n    is a boolean value indicating whether\n      it has already been called.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    To indicate that you\'d like to use HTML5\n    <tt>\n     pushState\n    </tt>\n    support in\n      your application, use\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.history.start({pushState: true})\n    </tt>\n    .\n      If you\'d like to use\n    <tt>\n     pushState\n    </tt>\n    , but have browsers that don\'t support\n      it natively use full page refreshes instead, you can add\n    <tt>\n     {hashChange: false}\n    </tt>\n    to the options.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    If your application is not being served from the root url\n    <tt>\n     /\n    </tt>\n    of your\n      domain, be sure to tell History where the root really is, as an option:\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.history.start({pushState: true, root: "/public/search/"})\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    When called, if a route succeeds with a match for the current URL,\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.history.start()\n    </tt>\n    returns\n    <tt>\n     true\n    </tt>\n    . If no defined\n      route matches the current URL, it returns\n    <tt>\n     false\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    If the server has already rendered the entire page, and you don\'t want the\n      initial route to trigger when starting History, pass\n    <tt>\n     silent: true\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Because hash-based history in Internet Explorer relies on an\n    <tt>\n     &lt;iframe&gt;\n    </tt>\n    , be sure to only call\n    <tt>\n     start()\n    </tt>\n    after the DOM\n      is ready.\n   </p>\n   <pre>$(function(){\n  new WorkspaceRouter();\n  new HelpPaneRouter();\n  Backbone.history.start({pushState: true});\n});\n</pre>\n   <h2 id="Sync">\n    Backbone.sync\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     Backbone.sync\n    </b>\n    is the function that Backbone calls every time it\n      attempts to read or save a model to the server. By default, it uses\n    <tt>\n     jQuery.ajax\n    </tt>\n    to make a RESTful JSON request and returns a\n    <a href="http://api.jquery.com/jQuery.ajax/#jqXHR">\n     jqXHR\n    </a>\n    . You can override\n      it in order to use a different persistence strategy, such as WebSockets,\n      XML transport, or Local Storage.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The method signature of\n    <b>\n     Backbone.sync\n    </b>\n    is\n    <tt>\n     sync(method, model, [options])\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <ul>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      method\n     </b>\n     \xe2\x80\x93 the CRUD method (\n     <tt>\n      "create"\n     </tt>\n     ,\n     <tt>\n      "read"\n     </tt>\n     ,\n     <tt>\n      "update"\n     </tt>\n     , or\n     <tt>\n      "delete"\n     </tt>\n     )\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      model\n     </b>\n     \xe2\x80\x93 the model to be saved (or collection to be read)\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      options\n     </b>\n     \xe2\x80\x93 success and error callbacks, and all other jQuery request options\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   <p>\n    With the default implementation, when\n    <b>\n     Backbone.sync\n    </b>\n    sends up a request to save\n      a model, its attributes will be passed, serialized as JSON, and sent in the HTTP body\n      with content-type\n    <tt>\n     application/json\n    </tt>\n    . When returning a JSON response,\n      send down the attributes of the  model that have been changed by the server, and need\n      to be updated on the client. When responding to a\n    <tt>\n     "read"\n    </tt>\n    request from a collection\n      (\n    <a href="#Collection-fetch">\n     Collection#fetch\n    </a>\n    ), send down an array\n      of model attribute objects.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Whenever a model or collection begins a\n    <b>\n     sync\n    </b>\n    with the server, a\n    <tt>\n     "request"\n    </tt>\n    event is emitted. If the request completes successfully\n      you\'ll get a\n    <tt>\n     "sync"\n    </tt>\n    event, and an\n    <tt>\n     "error"\n    </tt>\n    event if not.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The\n    <b>\n     sync\n    </b>\n    function may be overriden globally as\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.sync\n    </tt>\n    ,\n      or at a finer-grained level, by adding a\n    <tt>\n     sync\n    </tt>\n    function to a Backbone\n      collection or to an individual model.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The default\n    <b>\n     sync\n    </b>\n    handler maps CRUD to REST like so:\n   </p>\n   <ul>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      create \xe2\x86\x92 POST\n     </b>\n     <tt>\n      /collection\n     </tt>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      read \xe2\x86\x92 GET\n     </b>\n     <tt>\n      /collection[/id]\n     </tt>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      update \xe2\x86\x92 PUT\n     </b>\n     <tt>\n      /collection/id\n     </tt>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      patch \xe2\x86\x92 PATCH\n     </b>\n     <tt>\n      /collection/id\n     </tt>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      delete \xe2\x86\x92 DELETE\n     </b>\n     <tt>\n      /collection/id\n     </tt>\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   <p>\n    As an example, a Rails handler responding to an\n    <tt>\n     "update"\n    </tt>\n    call from\n    <tt>\n     Backbone\n    </tt>\n    might look like this:\n    <i>\n     (In real code, never use\n    </i>\n    <tt>\n     update_attributes\n    </tt>\n    <i>\n     blindly, and always whitelist the attributes\n      you allow to be changed.)\n    </i>\n   </p>\n   <pre>def update\n  account = Account.find params[:id]\n  account.update_attributes params\n  render :json =&gt; account\nend\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    One more tip for integrating Rails versions prior to 3.1 is to disable\n      the default namespacing for\n    <tt>\n     to_json\n    </tt>\n    calls on models by setting\n    <tt>\n     ActiveRecord::Base.include_root_in_json = false\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p id="Sync-ajax">\n    <b class="header">\n     ajax\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     Backbone.ajax = function(request) { ... };\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    If you want to use a custom AJAX function, or your endpoint doesn\'t support\n      the\n    <a href="http://api.jquery.com/jQuery.ajax/">\n     jQuery.ajax\n    </a>\n    API\n      and you need to tweak things, you can do so by setting\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.ajax\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Sync-emulateHTTP">\n    <b class="header">\n     emulateHTTP\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     Backbone.emulateHTTP = true\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    If you want to work with a legacy web server that doesn\'t support Backbone\'s\n      default REST/HTTP approach, you may choose to turn on\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.emulateHTTP\n    </tt>\n    .\n      Setting this option will fake\n    <tt>\n     PUT\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     PATCH\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     DELETE\n    </tt>\n    requests with\n      a HTTP\n    <tt>\n     POST\n    </tt>\n    , setting the\n    <tt>\n     X-HTTP-Method-Override\n    </tt>\n    header\n      with the true method. If\n    <tt>\n     emulateJSON\n    </tt>\n    is also on, the true method\n      will be passed as an additional\n    <tt>\n     _method\n    </tt>\n    parameter.\n   </p>\n   <pre>Backbone.emulateHTTP = true;\n\nmodel.save();  // POST to "/collection/id", with "_method=PUT" + header.\n</pre>\n   <p id="Sync-emulateJSON">\n    <b class="header">\n     emulateJSON\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     Backbone.emulateJSON = true\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    If you\'re working with a legacy web server that can\'t handle requests\n      encoded as\n    <tt>\n     application/json\n    </tt>\n    , setting\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.emulateJSON = true;\n    </tt>\n    will cause the JSON to be serialized under a\n    <tt>\n     model\n    </tt>\n    parameter, and\n      the request to be made with a\n    <tt>\n     application/x-www-form-urlencoded\n    </tt>\n    MIME type, as if from an HTML form.\n   </p>\n   <h2 id="View">\n    Backbone.View\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    Backbone views are almost more convention than they are code \xe2\x80\x94 they\n      don\'t determine anything about your HTML or CSS for you, and can be used\n      with any JavaScript templating library.\n      The general idea is to organize your interface into logical views,\n      backed by models, each of which can be updated independently when the\n      model changes, without having to redraw the page. Instead of digging into\n      a JSON object, looking up an element in the DOM, and updating the HTML by hand,\n      you can bind your view\'s\n    <tt>\n     render\n    </tt>\n    function to the model\'s\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event \xe2\x80\x94 and now everywhere that\n      model data is displayed in the UI, it is always immediately up to date.\n   </p>\n   <p id="View-extend">\n    <b class="header">\n     extend\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     Backbone.View.extend(properties, [classProperties])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Get started with views by creating a custom view class. You\'ll want to\n      override the\n    <a href="#View-render">\n     render\n    </a>\n    function, specify your\n      declarative\n    <a href="#View-delegateEvents">\n     events\n    </a>\n    , and perhaps the\n    <tt>\n     tagName\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     className\n    </tt>\n    , or\n    <tt>\n     id\n    </tt>\n    of the View\'s root\n      element.\n   </p>\n   <pre>var DocumentRow = Backbone.View.extend({\n\n  tagName: "li",\n\n  className: "document-row",\n\n  events: {\n    "click .icon":          "open",\n    "click .button.edit":   "openEditDialog",\n    "click .button.delete": "destroy"\n  },\n\n  initialize: function() {\n    this.listenTo(this.model, "change", this.render);\n  },\n\n  render: function() {\n    ...\n  }\n\n});\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    Properties like\n    <tt>\n     tagName\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     id\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     className\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     el\n    </tt>\n    , and\n    <tt>\n     events\n    </tt>\n    may also be defined as a function, if\n      you want to wait to define them until runtime.\n   </p>\n   <p id="View-constructor">\n    <b class="header">\n     constructor / initialize\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     new View([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    There are several special\n      options that, if passed, will be attached directly to the view:\n    <tt>\n     model\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     collection\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     el\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     id\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     className\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     tagName\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     attributes\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     events\n    </tt>\n    .\n      If the view defines an\n    <b>\n     initialize\n    </b>\n    function, it will be called when\n      the view is first created.
