</small>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/compare/0.3.2...0.3.3">\n     Diff\n    </a>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="http://htmlpreview.github.com/?https://raw.github.com/jashkenas/backbone/0.3.3/index.html">\n     Docs\n    </a>\n    <br/>\n    Backbone.js now supports\n    <a href="http://zeptojs.com">\n efficiently handle\n      attributes intended for HTML interpolation. When trying to persist a model,\n      failed requests will now trigger an\n    <tt>\n     "error"\n    </tt>\n    event. The\n      ubiquitous\n    <tt>\n     options\n    </tt>\n    argument is now passed as the final argument\n      to all\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    events.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b class="header">\n     0.3.2\n    </b>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <small>\n     <i>\n      Nov 23, 2010\n     </i>\n    </small>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/compare/0.3.1...0.3.2">\n     Diff\n    </a>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="http://htmlpreview.github.com/?https://raw.github.com/jashkenas/backbone/0.3.2/index.html">\n     Docs\n    </a>\n    <br/>\n    Bugfix for IE7 + iframe-based "hashchange" events.\n    <tt>\n     sync\n    </tt>\n    may now be\n      overridden on a per-model, or per-collection basis. Fixed recursion error\n      when calling\n    <tt>\n     save\n    </tt>\n    with no changed attributes, within a\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b class="header">\n     0.3.1\n    </b>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <small>\n     <i>\n      Nov 15, 2010\n     </i>\n    </small>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/compare/0.3.0...0.3.1">\n     Diff\n    </a>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="http://htmlpreview.github.com/?https://raw.github.com/jashkenas/backbone/0.3.1/index.html">\n     Docs\n    </a>\n    <br/>\n    All\n    <tt>\n     "add"\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     "remove"\n    </tt>\n    events are now sent through the\n      model, so that views can listen for them without having to know about the\n      collection. Added a\n    <tt>\n     remove\n    </tt>\n    method to\n    <a href="#View">\n     Backbone.View\n    </a>\n    .\n    <tt>\n     toJSON\n    </tt>\n    is no longer called at all for\n    <tt>\n     \'read\'\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     \'delete\'\n    </tt>\n    requests.\n      Backbone routes are now able to load empty URL fragments.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b class="header">\n     0.3.0\n    </b>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <small>\n     <i>\n      Nov 9, 2010\n     </i>\n    </small>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/compare/0.2.0...0.3.0">\n     Diff\n    </a>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="http://htmlpreview.github.com/?https://raw.github.com/jashkenas/backbone/0.3.0/index.html">\n     Docs\n    </a>\n    <br/>\n    Backbone now has\n    <a href="#Controller">\n     Controllers\n    </a>\n    and\n    <a href="#History">\n     History\n    </a>\n    , for doing client-side routing based on\n      URL fragments.\n      Added\n    <tt>\n     emulateHTTP\n    </tt>\n    to provide support for legacy servers that don\'t\n      do\n    <tt>\n     PUT\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     DELETE\n    </tt>\n    .\n      Added\n    <tt>\n     emulateJSON\n    </tt>\n    for servers that can\'t accept\n    <tt>\n     application/json\n    </tt>\n    encoded requests.\n      Added\n    <a href="#Model-clear">\n     Model#clear\n    </a>\n    , which removes all attributes\n      from a model.\n      All Backbone classes may now be seamlessly inherited by CoffeeScript classes.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b class="header">\n     0.2.0\n    </b>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <small>\n     <i>\n      Oct 25, 2010\n     </i>\n    </small>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/compare/0.1.2...0.2.0">\n     Diff\n    </a>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="http://htmlpreview.github.com/?https://raw.github.com/jashkenas/backbone/0.2.0/index.html">\n     Docs\n    </a>\n    <br/>\n    Instead of requiring server responses to be namespaced under a\n    <tt>\n     model\n    </tt>\n    key, now you can define your own\n    <a href="#Model-parse">\n     parse\n    </a>\n    method\n      to convert responses into attributes for Models and Collections.\n      The old\n    <tt>\n     handleEvents\n    </tt>\n    function is now named\n    <a href="#View-delegateEvents">\n     delegateEvents\n    </a>\n    , and is automatically\n      called as part of the View\'s constructor.\n      Added a\n    <a href="#Collection-toJSON">\n     toJSON\n    </a>\n    function to Collections.\n      Added\n    <a href="#Collection-chain">\n     Underscore\'s chain\n    </a>\n    to Collections.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b class="header">\n     0.1.2\n    </b>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <small>\n     <i>\n      Oct 19, 2010\n     </i>\n    </small>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/compare/0.1.1...0.1.2">\n     Diff\n    </a>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="http://htmlpreview.github.com/?https://raw.github.com/jashkenas/backbone/0.1.2/index.html">\n     Docs\n    </a>\n    <br/>\n    Added a\n    <a href="#Model-fetch">\n     Model#fetch\n    </a>\n    method for refreshing the\n      attributes of single model from the server.\n      An\n    <tt>\n     error\n    </tt>\n    callback may now be passed to\n    <tt>\n     set\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     save\n    </tt>\n    as an option, which will be invoked if validation fails, overriding the\n    <tt>\n     "error"\n    </tt>\n    event.\n      You can now tell backbone to use the\n    <tt>\n     _method\n    </tt>\n    hack instead of HTTP\n      methods by setting\n    <tt>\n     Backbone.emulateHTTP = true\n    </tt>\n    .\n      Existing Model and Collection data is no longer sent up unnecessarily with\n    <tt>\n     GET\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     DELETE\n    </tt>\n    requests. Added a\n    <tt>\n     rake lint\n    </tt>\n    task.\n      Backbone is now published as an\n    <a href="http://npmjs.org">\n     NPM\n    </a>\n    module.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b class="header">\n     0.1.1\n    </b>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <small>\n     <i>\n      Oct 14, 2010\n     </i>\n    </small>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/compare/0.1.0...0.1.1">\n     Diff\n    </a>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a href="http://htmlpreview.github.com/?https://raw.github.com/jashkenas/backbone/0.1.1/index.html">\n     Docs\n    </a>\n    <br/>\n    Added a convention for\n    <tt>\n     initialize\n    </tt>\n    functions to be called\n      upon instance construction, if defined. Documentation tweaks.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b class="header">\n     0.1.0\n    </b>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <small>\n     <i>\n      Oct 13, 2010\n     </i>\n    </small>\n    \xe2\x80\x94\n    <a   </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-blossom">\n      Blossom\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-trello">\n      Trello\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     \xe2\x80\x93\n     <a href="#examples-tzigla">\n      Tzigla\n     </a>\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   <a class="toc_title" href="#changelog">\n    Change Log\n   </a>\n  </div>\n  <div class="container">\n   <p>\n    <img alt="Backbone.js" id="logo" src="docs/images/backbone.png"/>\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Backbone.js gives structure to web applications\n      by providing\n    <b>\n     models\n    </b>\n    with key-value binding and custom events,\n    <b>\n     collections\n    </b>\n    with a rich API of enumerable functions,\n    <b>\n     views\n    </b>\n    with declarative event handling, and connects it all to your\n      existing API over a RESTful JSON interface.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The project is\n    <a href="http://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/">\n     hosted on GitHub\n    </a>\n    ,\n      and the\n    <a href="docs/backbone.html">\n     annotated source code\n    </a>\n    is available,\n      as well as an online\n    <a href="test/">\n     test suite\n    </a>\n    ,\n      an\n    <a href="examples/todos/index.html">\n     example application\n    </a>\n    ,\n      a\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/wiki/Tutorials%2C-blog-posts-and-example-sites">\n     list of tutorials\n    </a>\n    and a\n    <a href="#examples">\n     long list of real-world projects\n    </a>\n    that use Backbone.\n      Backbone is available for use under the\n    <a href="http://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/blob/master/LICENSE">\n     MIT software license\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    You can report bugs and discuss features on the\n    <a href="http://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/issues">\n     GitHub issues page\n    </a>\n    ,\n      on Freenode IRC in the\n    <tt>\n     #documentcloud\n    </tt>\n    channel, post questions to the\n    <a href="https://groups.google.com/forum/#!forum/backbonejs">\n     Google Group\n    </a>\n    ,\n      add pages to the\n    <a href="https://github.com/jashkenas/backbone/wiki">\n     wiki\n    </a>\n    or send tweets to\n    <a href="http://twitter.com/documentcloud">\n     @documentcloud\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <i>\n     Backbone is an open-source component of\n     <a href="http://documentcloud.org/">\n      DocumentCloud\n     </a>\n     .\n    </i>\n   </p>\n   <h2 id="downloads">\n    Downloads &amp; Dependencies\n    <span class="interface" style="padding-left: 7px; font-size:11px; font-weight: normal;">\n     (Right-click, and use "Save As")\n    </span>\n   </h2>\n   <table>\n    <tbody>\n     <tr>\n      <td>\n       <a class="punch" href="backbone.js">\n        Development Version (1.1.2)\n       </a>\n      </td>\n      <td class="text">\n       <i>\n        60kb, Full source, tons of comments\n       </i>\n      </td>\n     </tr>\n     <tr>\n      <td>\n       <a class="punch" href="backbone-min.js">\n        Production Version (1.1.2)\n       </a>\n      </td>\n      <td class="text" style="line-height: 16px;">\n       <i>\n        6.5kb, Packed and gzipped\n       </i>\n       <br/>\n       <small>\n        (\n        <a href="backbone-min.map">\n         Source Map\n        </a>\n        )\n       </small>\n      </td>\n     </tr>\n     <tr>\n      <td>\n       <a class="punch" href="https://raw.github.com/jashkenas/backbone/master/backbone.js">\n        Edge Version (master)\n       </a>\n      </td>\n      <td>\n       <i>\n        Unreleased, use at your own risk\n       </i>\n       <a class="travis-badge" href="https://travis-ci.org/jashkenas/backbone">\n        <img src="https://travis-ci.org/jashkenas/backbone.png"/>\n       </a>\n      </td>\n     </tr>\n    </tbody>\n   </table>\n   <p>\n    Backbone\'s only hard dependency is\n    <a href="http://underscorejs.org/">\n     Underscore.js\n    </a>\n    <small>\n     ( &gt;= 1.5.0)\n    </small>\n    .\n      For RESTful persistence, history support via\n    <a href="#Router">\n     Backbone.Router\n    </a>\n    and DOM manipulation with\n    <a href="#View">\n     Backbone.View\n    </a>\n    , include\n    <b>\n     <a href="http://jquery.com">\n      jQuery\n     </a>\n    </b>\n    , and\n    <b>\n     <a href="https://github.com/douglascrockford/JSON-js">\n      json2.js\n     </a>\n    </b>\n    for older\n      Internet Explorer support.\n    <i>\n     (Mimics of the Underscore and jQuery APIs, such as\n     <a href="http://lodash.com">\n      Lo-Dash\n     </a>\n     and\n     <a href="http://zeptojs.com">\n      Zepto\n     </a>\n     , will\n      also tend to work, with varying degrees of compatibility.)\n    </i>\n   </p>\n   <h2 id="introduction">\n    Introduction\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    When working on a web application that involves a lot of JavaScript, one\n      of the first things you learn is to stop tying your data to the DOM. It\'s all\n      too easy to create JavaScript applications that end up as tangled piles of\n      jQuery selectors and callbacks, all trying frantically to keep data in\n      sync between the HTML UI, your JavaScript logic, and the database on your\n      server. For rich client-side applications, a more structured approach\n      is often helpful.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    With Backbone, you represent your data as\n    <a href="#Model">\n     Models\n    </a>\n    , which can be created, validated, destroyed,\n      and saved to the server. Whenever a UI action causes an attribute of\n      a model to change, the model triggers a\n    <i>\n     "change"\n    </i>\n    event; all\n      the\n    <a href="#View">\n     Views\n    </a>\n    that display the model\'s state can be notified of the\n      change, so that they are able to respond accordingly, re-rendering themselves with\n      the new information. In a finished Backbone app, you don\'t have to write the glue\n      code that looks into the DOM to find an element with a specific\n    <i>\n     id\n    </i>\n    ,\n      and update the HTML manually\n      \xe2\x80\x94 when the model changes, the views simply update themselves.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Philosophically, Backbone is an attempt to discover the minimal set\n      of data-structuring (models and collections) and user interface (views\n      and URLs) primitives that are generally useful when building web applications with\n      JavaScript. In an ecosystem where overarching, decides-everything-for-you\n      frameworks are commonplace, and many libraries require your site to be\n      reorganized to suit their look, feel, and default behavior \xe2\x80\x94 Backbone should\n      continue to be a tool that gives you the\n    <i>\n     freedom\n    </i>\n    to design the full\n      experience of your web application.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    If you\'re new here, and aren\'t yet quite sure what Backbone is for, start by\n      browsing the\n    <a href="#examples">\n     list of Backbone-based projects\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Many of the examples that follow are runnable. Click the\n    <i>\n     play\n    </i>\n    button\n      to execute them.\n   </p>\n   <h2 id="upgrading">\n    Upgrading to 1.1\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    Backbone\n    <b>\n     1.1\n    </b>\n    should be a fairly painless upgrade from the\n    <b>\n     0.9.X\n    </b>\n    series. If you\'re upgrading from an older version, be sure to check out the\n    <a href="#changelog">\n     change log\n    </a>\n    . In brief, a few of the larger breaking\n      changes are:\n   </p>\n   <ul>\n    <li>\n     If you want to smartly update the contents of a Collection,\n        adding new models, removing missing ones, and merging those already present,\n        you now call\n     <a href="#Collection-set">\n      set\n     </a>\n     (previously named "update"),\n        a similar operation to calling\n     <tt>\n      set\n     </tt>\n     on a Model. This is now the\n        default when you call\n     <a href="#Collection-fetch">\n      fetch\n     </a>\n     on a collection.\n        To get the old behavior, pass\n     <tt>\n      {reset: true}\n     </tt>\n     .\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     If you have characters in your URL segments that require URL encoding,\n        Backbone will now decode them for you (normalizing the behavior\n        cross-browser) before your route handlers receive them as arguments.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     In\n     <b>\n      0.9.x\n     </b>\n     , Backbone events gained two new methods:\n     <a href="#Events-listenTo">\n      listenTo\n     </a>\n     and\n     <a href="#Events-stopListening">\n      stopListening\n     </a>\n     , which make it easier\n        to create Views that have all of their observers unbound when you\n        want to\n     <a href="#View-remove">\n      remove\n     </a>\n     the view.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     Model validation is now only enforced by default in\n     <a href="#Model-save">\n      save\n     </a>\n     \xe2\x80\x94 not in\n     <a href="#Model-set">\n      set\n     </a>\n     unless the\n     <tt>\n      {validate:true}\n     </tt>\n     option is passed. Model validation now fires an\n     <tt>\n      "invalid"\n     </tt>\n     event instead of\n     <tt>\n      "error"\n     </tt>\n     .\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     In 1.1, Backbone Views no longer have the\n     <tt>\n      options\n     </tt>\n     argument\n        attached as\n     <tt>\n      this.options\n     </tt>\n     automatically. Feel free to continue\n        attaching it if you like.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     In 1.1, The\n     <b>\n      Collection\n     </b>\n     methods\n     <tt>\n      add\n     </tt>\n     ,\n     <tt>\n      remove\n     </tt>\n     ,\n     <tt>\n      set\n     </tt>\n     ,\n     <tt>\n      push\n     </tt>\n     , and\n     <tt>\n      shift\n     </tt>\n     now return the model\n        (or models) added or removed from the collection.\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   <h2 id="Events">\n    Backbone.Events\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     Events\n    </b>\n    is a module that can be mixed in to any object, giving the\n      object the ability to bind and trigger custom named events. Events do not\n      have to be declared before they are bound, and may take passed arguments.\n      For example:\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var object = {};\n\n_.extend(object, Backbone.Events);\n\nobject.on("alert", function(msg) {\n  alert("Triggered " + msg);\n});\n\nobject.trigger("alert", "an event");\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    For example, to make a handy event dispatcher that can coordinate events\n      among different areas of your application:\n    <tt>\n     var dispatcher = _.clone(Backbone.Events)\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p id="Events-on">\n    <b class="header">\n     on\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.on(event, callback, [context])\n    </code>\n    <span class="alias">\n     Alias: bind\n    </span>\n    <br/>\n    Bind a\n    <b>\n     callback\n    </b>\n    function to an object. The callback will be invoked\n      whenever the\n    <b>\n     event\n    </b>\n    is fired.\n      If you have a large number of different events on a page, the convention is to use colons to\n      namespace them:\n    <tt>\n     "poll:start"\n    </tt>\n    , or\n    <tt>\n     "change:selection"\n    </tt>\n    .\n      The event string may also be a space-delimited list of several events...\n   </p>\n   <pre>book.on("change:title change:author", ...);\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    To supply a\n    <b>\n     context\n    </b>\n    value for\n    <tt>\n     this\n    </tt>\n    when the callback is invoked,\n      pass the optional third argument:\n    <tt>\n     model.on(\'change\', this.render, this)\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Callbacks bound to the special\n    <tt>\n     "all"\n    </tt>\n    event will be triggered when any event occurs, and are passed\n      the name of the event as the first argument. For example, to proxy all events\n      from one object to another:\n   </p>\n   <pre>proxy.on("all", function(eventName) {\n  object.trigger(eventName);\n});\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    All Backbone event methods also support an event map syntax, as an alternative\n      to positional arguments:\n   </p>\n   <pre>book.on({\n  "change:title": titleView.update,\n  "change:author": authorPane.update,\n  "destroy": bookView.remove\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Events-off">\n    <b class="header">\n     off\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.off([event], [callback], [context])\n    </code>\n    <span class="alias">\n     Alias: unbind\n    </span>\n    <br/>\n    Remove a previously-bound\n    <b>\n     callback\n    </b>\n    function from an object. If no\n    <b>\n     context\n    </b>\n    is specified, all of the versions of the callback with\n      different contexts will be removed. If no\n      callback is specified, all callbacks for the\n    <b>\n     event\n    </b>\n    will be\n      removed. If no event is specified, callbacks for\n    <i>\n     all\n    </i>\n    events\n      will be removed.\n   </p>\n   <pre>// Removes just the `onChange` callback.\nobject.off("change", onChange);\n\n// Removes all "change" callbacks.\nobject.off("change");\n\n// Removes the `onChange` callback for all events.\nobject.off(null, onChange);\n\n// Removes all callbacks for `context` for all events.\nobject.off(null, null, context);\n\n// Removes all callbacks on `object`.\nobject.off();\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    Note that calling\n    <tt>\n     model.off()\n    </tt>\n    , for example, will indeed remove\n    <i>\n     all\n    </i>\n    events\n      on the model \xe2\x80\x94 including events that Backbone uses for internal bookkeeping.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Events-trigger">\n    <b class="header">\n     trigger\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.trigger(event, [*args])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Trigger callbacks for the given\n    <b>\n     event\n    </b>\n    , or space-delimited list of events.\n      Subsequent arguments to\n    <b>\n     trigger\n    </b>\n    will be passed along to the\n      event callbacks.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Events-once">\n    <b class="header">\n     once\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.once(event, callback, [context])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Just like\n    <a href="#Events-on">\n     on\n    </a>\n    , but causes the bound callback to only\n      fire once before being removed. Handy for saying "the next time that X happens, do this".\n   </p>\n   <p id="Events-listenTo">\n    <b class="header">\n     listenTo\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.listenTo(other, event, callback)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Tell an\n    <b>\n     object\n    </b>\n    to listen to a particular event on an\n    <b>\n     other\n    </b>\n    object.  The advantage of using this form, instead of\n    <tt>\n     other.on(event,\n      callback, object)\n    </tt>\n    , is that\n    <b>\n     listenTo\n    </b>\n    allows the\n    <b>\n     object\n    </b>\n    to keep track of the events, and they can be removed all at once later\n      on.  The\n    <b>\n     callback\n    </b>\n    will always be called with\n    <b>\n     object\n    </b>\n    as\n      context.\n   </p>\n   <pre>view.listenTo(model, \'change\', view.render);\n</pre>\n   <p id="Events-stopListening">\n    <b class="header">\n     stopListening\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.stopListening([other], [event], [callback])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Tell an\n    <b>\n     object\n    </b>\n    to stop listening to events. Either call\n    <b>\n     stopListening\n    </b>\n    with no arguments to have the\n    <b>\n     object\n    </b>\n    remove\n      all of its\n    <a href="#Events-listenTo">\n     registered\n    </a>\n    callbacks ... or be more\n      precise by telling it to remove just the events it\'s listening to on a\n      specific object, or a specific event, or just a specific callback.\n   </p>\n   <pre>view.stopListening();\n\nview.stopListening(model);\n</pre>\n   <p id="Events-listenToOnce">\n    <b class="header">\n     listenToOnce\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     object.listenToOnce(other, event, callback)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Just like\n    <a href="#Events-listenTo">\n     listenTo\n    </a>\n    , but causes the bound\n      callback to only fire once before being removed.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Events-catalog">\n    <b class="header">\n     Catalog of Events\n    </b>\n    <br/>\n    Here\'s the complete list of built-in Backbone events, with arguments.\n      You\'re also free to trigger your own events on Models, Collections and\n      Views as you see fit. The\n    <tt>\n     Backbone\n    </tt>\n    object itself mixes in\n    <tt>\n     Events\n    </tt>\n    ,\n      and can be used to emit any global events that your application needs.\n   </p>\n   <ul class="small">\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "add"\n     </b>\n     (model, collection, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model is added to a collection.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "remove"\n     </b>\n     (model, collection, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model is removed from a collection.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "reset"\n     </b>\n     (collection, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when the collection\'s entire contents have been replaced.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "sort"\n     </b>\n     (collection, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when the collection has been re-sorted.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "change"\n     </b>\n     (model, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model\'s attributes have changed.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "change:[attribute]"\n     </b>\n     (model, value, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a specific attribute has been updated.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "destroy"\n     </b>\n     (model, collection, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model is\n     <a href="#Model-destroy">\n      destroyed\n     </a>\n     .\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "request"\n     </b>\n     (model_or_collection, xhr, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model or collection has started a request to the server.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "sync"\n     </b>\n     (model_or_collection, resp, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model or collection has been successfully synced with the server.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "error"\n     </b>\n     (model_or_collection, resp, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when model\'s or collection\'s request to remote server has failed.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "invalid"\n     </b>\n     (model, error, options) \xe2\x80\x94 when a model\'s\n     <a href="#Model-validate">\n      validation\n     </a>\n     fails on the client.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "route:[name]"\n     </b>\n     (params) \xe2\x80\x94 Fired by the router when a specific route is matched.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "route"\n     </b>\n     (route, params) \xe2\x80\x94 Fired by the router when\n     <i>\n      any\n     </i>\n     route has been matched.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "route"\n     </b>\n     (router, route, params) \xe2\x80\x94 Fired by history when\n     <i>\n      any\n     </i>\n     route has been matched.\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <b>\n      "all"\n     </b>\n     \xe2\x80\x94 this special event fires for\n     <i>\n      any\n     </i>\n     triggered event, passing the event name as the first argument.\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   <p>\n    Generally speaking, when calling a function that emits an event\n      (\n    <tt>\n     model.set\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     collection.add\n    </tt>\n    , and so on...),\n      if you\'d like to prevent the event from being triggered, you may pass\n    <tt>\n     {silent: true}\n    </tt>\n    as an option. Note that this is\n    <i>\n     rarely\n    </i>\n    ,\n      perhaps even never, a good idea. Passing through a specific flag\n      in the options for your event callback to look at, and choose to ignore,\n      will usually work out better.\n   </p>\n   <h2 id="Model">\n    Backbone.Model\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     Models\n    </b>\n    are the heart of any JavaScript application, containing\n      the interactive data as well as a large part of the logic surrounding it:\n      conversions, validations, computed properties, and access control. You\n      extend\n    <b>\n     Backbone.Model\n    </b>\n    with your domain-specific methods, and\n    <b>\n     Model\n    </b>\n    provides a basic set of functionality for managing changes.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    The following is a contrived example, but it demonstrates defining a model\n      with a custom method, setting an attribute, and firing an event keyed\n      to changes in that specific attribute.\n      After running this code once,\n    <tt>\n     sidebar\n    </tt>\n    will be\n      available in your browser\'s console, so you can play around with it.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var Sidebar = Backbone.Model.extend({\n  promptColor: function() {\n    var cssColor = prompt("Please enter a CSS color:");\n    this.set({color: cssColor});\n  }\n});\n\nwindow.sidebar = new Sidebar;\n\nsidebar.on(\'change:color\', function(model, color) {\n  $(\'#sidebar\').css({background: color});\n});\n\nsidebar.set({color: \'white\'});\n\nsidebar.promptColor();\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-extend">\n    <b class="header">\n     extend\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     Backbone.Model.extend(properties, [classProperties])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    To create a\n    <b>\n     Model\n    </b>\n    class of your own, you extend\n    <b>\n     Backbone.Model\n    </b>\n    and provide instance\n    <b>\n     properties\n    </b>\n    , as well as optional\n    <b>\n     classProperties\n    </b>\n    to be attached directly to the constructor function.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    <b>\n     extend\n    </b>\n    correctly sets up the prototype chain, so subclasses created\n      with\n    <b>\n     extend\n    </b>\n    can be further extended and subclassed as far as you like.\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Note = Backbone.Model.extend({\n\n  initialize: function() { ... },\n\n  author: function() { ... },\n\n  coordinates: function() { ... },\n\n  allowedToEdit: function(account) {\n    return true;\n  }\n\n});\n\nvar PrivateNote = Note.extend({\n\n  allowedToEdit: function(account) {\n    return account.owns(this);\n  }\n\n});\n</pre>\n   <p class="warning">\n    Brief aside on\n    <tt>\n     super\n    </tt>\n    : JavaScript does not provide\n        a simple way to call super \xe2\x80\x94 the function of the same name defined\n        higher on the prototype chain. If you override a core function like\n    <tt>\n     set\n    </tt>\n    , or\n    <tt>\n     save\n    </tt>\n    , and you want to invoke the\n        parent object\'s implementation, you\'ll have to explicitly call it, along these lines:\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Note = Backbone.Model.extend({\n  set: function(attributes, options) {\n    Backbone.Model.prototype.set.apply(this, arguments);\n    ...\n  }\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-constructor">\n    <b class="header">\n     constructor / initialize\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     new Model([attributes], [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    When creating an instance of a model, you can pass in the initial values\n      of the\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    , which will be\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    on the\n      model. If you define an\n    <b>\n     initialize\n    </b>\n    function, it will be invoked when\n      the model is created.\n   </p>\n   <pre>new Book({\n  title: "One Thousand and One Nights",\n  author: "Scheherazade"\n});\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    In rare cases, if you\'re looking to get fancy,\n      you may want to override\n    <b>\n     constructor\n    </b>\n    , which allows\n      you to replace the actual constructor function for your model.\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Library = Backbone.Model.extend({\n  constructor: function() {\n    this.books = new Books();\n    Backbone.Model.apply(this, arguments);\n  },\n  parse: function(data, options) {\n    this.books.reset(data.books);\n    return data.library;\n  }\n});\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    If you pass a\n    <tt>\n     {collection: ...}\n    </tt>\n    as the\n    <b>\n     options\n    </b>\n    , the model\n      gains a\n    <tt>\n     collection\n    </tt>\n    property that will be used to indicate which\n      collection the model belongs to, and is used to help compute the model\'s\n    <a href="#Model-url">\n     url\n    </a>\n    . The\n    <tt>\n     model.collection\n    </tt>\n    property is\n      normally created automatically when you first add a model to a collection.\n      Note that the reverse is not true, as passing this option to the constructor\n      will not automatically add the model to the collection. Useful, sometimes.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    If\n    <tt>\n     {parse: true}\n    </tt>\n    is passed as an\n    <b>\n     option\n    </b>\n    , the\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    will first be converted by\n    <a href="#Model-parse">\n     parse\n    </a>\n    before being\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    on the model.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-get">\n    <b class="header">\n     get\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.get(attribute)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Get the current value of an attribute from the model. For example:\n    <tt>\n     note.get("title")\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-set">\n    <b class="header">\n     set\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.set(attributes, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Set a hash of attributes (one or many) on the model. If any of the attributes\n      change the model\'s state, a\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event will be triggered on the model.\n      Change events for specific attributes are also triggered, and you can bind\n      to those as well, for example:\n    <tt>\n     change:title\n    </tt>\n    , and\n    <tt>\n     change:content\n    </tt>\n    .\n      You may also pass individual keys and values.\n   </p>\n   <pre>note.set({title: "March 20", content: "In his eyes she eclipses..."});\n\nbook.set("title", "A Scandal in Bohemia");\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-escape">\n    <b class="header">\n     escape\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.escape(attribute)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Similar to\n    <a href="#Model-get">\n     get\n    </a>\n    , but returns the HTML-escaped version\n      of a model\'s attribute. If you\'re interpolating data from the model into\n      HTML, using\n    <b>\n     escape\n    </b>\n    to retrieve attributes will prevent\n    <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cross-site_scripting">\n     XSS\n    </a>\n    attacks.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var hacker = new Backbone.Model({\n  name: "&lt;script&gt;alert(\'xss\')&lt;/script&gt;"\n});\n\nalert(hacker.escape(\'name\'));\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-has">\n    <b class="header">\n     has\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.has(attribute)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Returns\n    <tt>\n     true\n    </tt>\n    if the attribute is set to a non-null or non-undefined\n      value.\n   </p>\n   <pre>if (note.has("title")) {\n  ...\n}\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-unset">\n    <b class="header">\n     unset\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.unset(attribute, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Remove an attribute by deleting it from the internal attributes hash.\n      Fires a\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event unless\n    <tt>\n     silent\n    </tt>\n    is passed as an option.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-clear">\n    <b class="header">\n     clear\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.clear([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Removes all attributes from the model, including the\n    <tt>\n     id\n    </tt>\n    attribute. Fires a\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event unless\n    <tt>\n     silent\n    </tt>\n    is passed as an option.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-id">\n    <b class="header">\n     id\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.id\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    A special property of models, the\n    <b>\n     id\n    </b>\n    is an arbitrary string\n      (integer id or UUID). If you set the\n    <b>\n     id\n    </b>\n    in the\n      attributes hash, it will be copied onto the model as a direct property.\n      Models can be retrieved by id from collections, and the id is used to generate\n      model URLs by default.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-idAttribute">\n    <b class="header">\n     idAttribute\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.idAttribute\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    A model\'s unique identifier is stored under the\n    <tt>\n     id\n    </tt>\n    attribute.\n      If you\'re directly communicating with a backend (CouchDB, MongoDB) that uses\n      a different unique key, you may set a Model\'s\n    <tt>\n     idAttribute\n    </tt>\n    to\n      transparently map from that key to\n    <tt>\n     id\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var Meal = Backbone.Model.extend({\n  idAttribute: "_id"\n});\n\nvar cake = new Meal({ _id: 1, name: "Cake" });\nalert("Cake id: " + cake.id);\n</pre>\n   <p>\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-cid">\n    <b class="header">\n     cid\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.cid\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    A special property of models, the\n    <b>\n     cid\n    </b>\n    or client id is a unique identifier\n      automatically assigned to all models when they\'re first created. Client ids\n      are handy when the model has not yet been saved to the server, and does not\n      yet have its eventual true\n    <b>\n     id\n    </b>\n    , but already needs to be visible in the UI.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-attributes">\n    <b class="header">\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.attributes\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    The\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    property is the internal hash containing the model\'s\n      state \xe2\x80\x94 usually (but not necessarily) a form of the JSON object\n      representing the model data on the server. It\'s often a straightforward\n      serialization of a row from the database, but it could also be client-side\n      computed state.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Please use\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    to update the\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    instead of modifying them directly. If you\'d like to retrieve and munge a\n      copy of the model\'s attributes, use\n    <tt>\n     _.clone(model.attributes)\n    </tt>\n    instead.\n   </p>\n   <p class="warning">\n    Due to the fact that\n    <a href="#Events">\n     Events\n    </a>\n    accepts space separated\n      lists of events, attribute names should not include spaces.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-changed">\n    <b class="header">\n     changed\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.changed\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    The\n    <b>\n     changed\n    </b>\n    property is the internal hash containing all the attributes\n      that have changed since the last\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    .\n      Please do not update\n    <b>\n     changed\n    </b>\n    directly since its state is internally maintained\n      by\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    . The\n      name of this method is a bit confusing, as it doesn\'t actually return a\n      JSON string \xe2\x80\x94 but I\'m afraid that it\'s the way that the\n    <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en/JSON#toJSON()_method">\n     JavaScript API for\n     <b>\n      JSON.stringify\n     </b>\n    </a>\n    works.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var artist = new Backbone.Model({\n  firstName: "Wassily",\n  lastName: "Kandinsky"\n});\n\nartist.set({birthday: "December 16, 1866"});\n\nalert(JSON.stringify(artist));\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-sync">\n    <b class="header">\n     sync\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.sync(method, model, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Uses\n    <a href="#Sync">\n     Backbone.sync\n    </a>\n    to persist the state of a model to\n      the server.  Can be overridden for custom behavior.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Model-fetch">\n    <b class="header">\n     fetch\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.fetch([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Resets the model\'s state from the server by delegating to\n    <a href="#Sync">\n     Backbone.sync\n    </a>\n    . Returns a\n    <a href="http://api.jquery.com/jQuery.ajax/#jqXHR">\n     jqXHR\n    </a>\n    .\n      Useful if the model has never\n      been populated with data, or if you\'d like to ensure that you have the\n      latest server state. A\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event will be triggered if the\n      server\'s state differs from the current attributes. Accepts\n    <tt>\n     success\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     error\n    </tt>\n    callbacks in the options hash, which\n      are both passed\n    <tt>\n     (model, response, options)\n    </tt>\n    as arguments.\n   </p>\n   <pre>// Poll every 10 seconds to keep the channel model up-to-date.\nsetInterval(function() {\n  channel.fetch();\n}, 10000);\n</pre>\n   <p id="Model-save">\n    <b class="header">\n     save\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     model.save([attributes], [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Save a model to your database (or alternative persistence layer),\n      by delegating to\n    <a href="#Sync">\n     Backbone.sync\n    </a>\n    .  Returns a\n    <a href="http://api.jquery.com/jQuery.ajax/#jqXHR">\n     jqXHR\n    </a>\n    if\n      validation is successful and\n    <tt>\n     false\n    </tt>\n    otherwise. The\n    <b>\n     attributes\n    </b>\n    hash (as in\n    <a href="#Model-set">\n     set\n    </a>\n    ) should contain the attributes\n      you\'d like to change \xe2\x80\x94 keys that aren\'t mentioned won\'t be altered \xe2\x80\x94 but,\n      a\n    <i>\n     complete representation\n    </i>\n    of the resource will be sent to the server.\n      As with\n    <tt>\n     set\n    </tt>\n    , you may pass individual keys and values instead of a hash.\n      If the model has a\n    <a href="#Model-validate">\n     validate\n    </a>\n    method, and validation fails, the model will not be saved. If the model\n    <a href="#Model-isNew">\n     isNew\n    </a>\n    , the save will be a\n    <tt>\n     "create"\n    </tt>\n    (HTTP\n    <tt>\n     POST\n    </tt>\n    ), if the model already\n      exists on the server, the save will be an\n    <tt>\n     "update"\n    </tt>\n    (HTTP\n    <tt>\n     PUT\n    </tt>\n    ).\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    If instead, you\'d only like the\n    <i>\n     changed\n    </i>\n    attributes to be sent to the\n      server, call\n    <tt>\n     model.save(attrs, {patch: true})\n    </tt>\n    . You\'ll get an HTTP\n    <tt>\n     PATCH\n    </tt>\n    request to the server with just the passed-in attributes.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Calling\n    <tt>\n     save\n    </tt>\n    with new attributes will cause a\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    event immediately, a\n    <tt>\n     "request"\n    </tt>\n    event as the Ajax request begins to\n      go to the server, and a\n    <tt>\n     "sync"\n    </tt>\n    event after the server has acknowledged\n      the successful change. By default\n    <b>\n     validate\n    </b>\n    is called before\n    <tt>\n     save\n    </tt>\n    , but can also be called before\n    <tt>\n     set\n    </tt>\n    if\n    <tt>\n     {validate:true}\n    </tt>\n    is passed. The\n    <b>\n     validate\n    </b>\n    method is passed\n      the model attributes, as well as the options from\n    <tt>\n     set\n    </tt>\n    or\n    <tt>\n     save\n    </tt>\n    .\n      If the attributes are valid, don\'t return anything from\n    <b>\n     validate\n    </b>\n    ;\n      if they are invalid, return an error of your choosing. It\n      can be as simple as a string error message to be displayed, or a complete\n      error object that describes the error programmatically. If\n    <b>\n     validate\n    </b>\n    returns an error,\n    <tt>\n     save\n    </tt>\n    will not continue, and the\n      model attributes will not be modified on the server.\n      Failed validations trigger an\n    <tt>\n     "invalid"\n    </tt>\n    event, and set the\n    <tt>\n     validationError\n    </tt>\n    property on the model with the value returned by\n      this method.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var Chapter = Backbone.Model.extend({\n  validate: function(attrs, options) {\n    if (attrs.end &lt; Useful for getting a\n      diff between versions of a model, or getting back to a valid state after\n      an error occurs.\n   </p>\n   <h2 id="Collection">\n    Backbone.Collection\n   </h2>\n   <p>\n    Collections are ordered sets of models. You can bind\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    events\n      to be notified when any model in the collection has been modified,\n      listen for\n    <tt>\n     "add"\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     "remove"\n    </tt>\n    events,\n    <tt>\n     fetch\n    </tt>\n    the collection from the server, and use a full suite of\n    <a href="#Collection-Underscore-Methods">\n     Underscore.js methods\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Any event that is triggered on a model in a collection will also be\n      triggered on the collection directly, for convenience.\n      This allows you to listen for changes to specific attributes in any\n      model in a collection, for example:\n    <tt>\n     documents.on("change:selected", ...)\n    </tt>\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-extend">\n    <b class="header">\n     extend\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     Backbone.Collection.extend(properties, [classProperties])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    To create a\n    <b>\n     Collection\n    </b>\n    class of your own, extend\n    <b>\n     Backbone.Collection\n    </b>\n    ,\n      providing instance\n    <b>\n     properties\n    </b>\n    , as well as optional\n    <b>\n     classProperties\n    </b>\n    to be attached\n      directly to the collection\'s constructor function.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-model">\n    <b class="header">\n     model\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.model\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Override this property to specify the model class that the collection\n      contains. If defined, you can pass raw attributes objects (and arrays) to\n    <a href="#Collection-add">\n     add\n    </a>\n    ,\n    <a href="#Collection-create">\n     create\n    </a>\n    ,\n      and\n    <a href="#Collection-reset">\n     reset\n    </a>\n    , and the attributes will be\n      converted into a model of the proper type.\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Library = Backbone.Collection.extend({\n  model: Book\n});\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    A collection can also contain polymorphic models by overriding this property\n      with a constructor that returns a model.\n   </p>\n   <pre>var Library = Backbone.Collection.extend({\n\n  model: function(attrs, options) {\n    if (condition) {\n      return new PublicDocument(attrs, options);\n    } else {\n      return new PrivateDocument(attrs, options);\n    }\n  }\n\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-constructor">\n    <b class="header">\n     constructor / initialize\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     new Backbone.Collection([models], [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    When creating a Collection, you may choose to pass in the initial array\n      of\n    <b>\n     models\n    </b>\n    .  The collection\'s\n    <a href="#Collection-comparator">\n     comparator\n    </a>\n    may be included as an option. Passing\n    <tt>\n     false\n    </tt>\n    as the\n      comparator option will prevent sorting. If you define an\n    <b>\n     initialize\n    </b>\n    function, it will be invoked when the collection is\n      created. There are a couple of options that, if provided, are attached to\n      the collection directly:\n    <tt>\n     model\n    </tt>\n    and\n    <tt>\n     comparator\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <pre>var tabs = new TabSet([tab1, tab2, tab3]);\nvar spaces = new Backbone.Collection([], {\n  model: Space\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-models">\n    <b class="header">\n     models\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.models\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Raw access to the JavaScript array of models inside of the collection. Usually you\'ll\n      want to use\n    <tt>\n     get\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     at\n    </tt>\n    , or the\n    <b>\n     Underscore methods\n    </b>\n    to access model objects, but occasionally a direct reference to the array\n      is desired.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-toJSON">\n    <b class="header">\n     toJSON\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.toJSON([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Return an array containing the attributes hash of each model\n      (via\n    <a href="#Model-toJSON">\n     toJSON\n    </a>\n    ) in the\n      collection. This can be used to serialize and persist the\n      collection as a whole. The name of this method is a bit confusing, because\n      it conforms to\n    <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/JSON/stringify#toJSON_behavior">\n     JavaScript\'s JSON API\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var collection = new Backbone.Collection([\n  {name: "Tim", age: 5},\n  {name: "Ida", age: 26},\n  {name: "Rob", age: 55}\n]);\n\nalert(JSON.stringify(collection));\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-sync">\n    <b class="header">\n     sync\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.sync(method, collection, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Uses\n    <a href="#Sync">\n     Backbone.sync\n    </a>\n    to persist the state of a\n      collection to the server.  Can be overridden for custom behavior.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-Underscore-Methods">\n    <b class="header">\n     Underscore Methods (28)\n    </b>\n    <br/>\n    Backbone proxies to\n    <b>\n     Underscore.js\n    </b>\n    to provide 28 iteration functions\n      on\n    <b>\n     Backbone.Collection\n    </b>\n    . <a href="http://underscorejs.org/#rest">\n      rest (tail)\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <a href="http://underscorejs.org/#last">\n      last\n     </a>\n    </li>\n    <li>\n     <a <a href="http://underscorejs.org/#chain">\n      chain\n     </a>\n    </li>\n   </ul>\n   <pre>books.each(function(book) {\n  book.publish();\n});\n\nvar titles = books.map(function(book) {\n  return book.get("title");\n});\n\nvar publishedBooks = books.filter(function(book) {\n  return book.get("published") === true;\n});\n\nvar alphabetical = books.sortBy(function(book) {\n  return book.author.get("name").toLowerCase();\n});\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-add">\n    <b class="header">\n     add\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.add(models, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Add a model (or an array of models) to the collection, firing an\n    <tt>\n     "add"\n    </tt>\n    event. If a\n    <a href="#Collection-model">\n     model\n    </a>\n    property is defined, you may also pass\n      raw attributes objects, and have them be vivified as instances of the model.\n      Returns the added (or preexisting, if duplicate) models.\n      Pass\n    <tt>\n     {at: index}\n    </tt>\n    to splice the model into the collection at the\n      specified\n    <tt>\n     index\n    </tt>\n    . If you\'re adding models to the collection that are\n    <i>\n     already\n    </i>\n    in the collection, they\'ll be ignored, unless you pass\n    <tt>\n     {merge: true}\n    </tt>\n    , in which case their attributes will be merged\n      into the corresponding models, firing any appropriate\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    events.\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var ships = new Backbone.Collection;\n\nships.on("add", function(ship) {\n  alert("Ahoy " + ship.get("name") + "!");\n});\n\nships.add([\n  {name: "Flying Dutchman"},\n  {name: "Black Pearl"}\n]);\n</pre>\n   <p class="warning">\n    Note that adding the same model (a model with the same\n    <tt>\n     id\n    </tt>\n    ) to\n      a collection more than once\n    <br/>\n    is a no-op.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-remove">\n    <b class="header">\n     remove\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.remove(models, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Remove a model (or an array of models) from the collection, and returns them.\n      Fires a\n    <tt>\n     "remove"\n    </tt>\n    event, which you can use\n    <tt>\n     silent\n    </tt>\n    to suppress.\n      The model\'s index before removal is available to listeners as\n    <tt>\n     options.index\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-reset">\n    <b class="header">\n     reset\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.reset([models], [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Adding and removing models one at a time is all well and good, but sometimes\n      you have so many models to change that you\'d rather just update the collection\n      in bulk. Use\n    <b>\n     reset\n    </b>\n    to replace a collection with a new list\n      of models (or attribute hashes), triggering a single\n    <tt>\n     "reset"\n    </tt>\n    event\n      at the end. Returns the newly-set models.\n      For convenience, within a\n    <tt>\n     "reset"\n    </tt>\n    event, the list of any\n      previous models is available as\n    <tt>\n     options.previousModels\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Here\'s an example using\n    <b>\n     reset\n    </b>\n    to bootstrap a collection during initial page load,\n      in a Rails application:\n   </p>\n   <pre>&lt;script&gt;\n  var accounts = new Backbone.Collection;\n  accounts.reset(&lt;%= @accounts.to_json %&gt;);\n&lt;/script&gt;\n</pre>\n   <p>\n    Calling\n    <tt>\n     collection.reset()\n    </tt>\n    without passing any models as arguments\n      will empty the entire collection.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-set">\n    <b class="header">\n     set\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.set(models, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    The\n    <b>\n     set\n    </b>\n    method performs a "smart" update of the collection\n      with the passed list of models. If a model in the list isn\'t yet in the\n      collection it will be added; if the model is already in the collection\n      its attributes will be merged; and if the collection contains any models that\n    <i>\n     aren\'t\n    </i>\n    present in the list, they\'ll be removed. All of the appropriate\n    <tt>\n     "add"\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     "remove"\n    </tt>\n    , and\n    <tt>\n     "change"\n    </tt>\n    events are fired\n      as this happens. Returns the touched models in the collection.\n      If you\'d like to customize the behavior, you can disable\n      it with options:\n    <tt>\n     {add: false}\n    </tt>\n    ,\n    <tt>\n     {remove: false}\n    </tt>\n    , or\n    <tt>\n     {merge: false}\n    </tt>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <pre>var vanHalen = new Backbone.Collection([eddie, alex, stone, roth]);\n\nvanHalen.set([eddie, alex, stone, hagar]);\n\n// Fires a "remove" event for roth, and an "add" event for "hagar".\n// Updates any of stone, alex, and eddie\'s attributes that may have\n// changed over the years.\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-get">\n    <b class="header">\n     get\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.get(id)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Get a model from a collection, specified by an\n    <a href="#Model-id">\n     id\n    </a>\n    ,\n      a\n    <a href="#Model-cid">\n     cid\n    </a>\n    , or by passing in a\n    <b>\n     model\n    </b>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <pre>var book = library.get(110);\n</pre>\n   <p id="Collection-at">\n    <b class="header">\n     at\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.at(index)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Get a model from a collection, specified by index. Useful if your collection\n      is sorted, and if your collection isn\'t sorted,\n    <b>\n     at\n    </b>\n    will still\n      retrieve models in insertion order.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-push">\n    <b class="header">\n     push\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.push(model, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Add a model at the end of a collection. Takes the same options as\n    <a href="#Collection-add">\n     add\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-pop">\n    <b class="header">\n     pop\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.pop([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Remove and return the last model from a collection. Takes the same options as\n    <a href="#Collection-remove">\n     remove\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-unshift">\n    <b class="header">\n     unshift\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.unshift(model, [options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Add a model at the beginning of a collection. Takes the same options as\n    <a href="#Collection-add">\n     add\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-shift">\n    <b class="header">\n     shift\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.shift([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Remove and return the first model from a collection. Takes the same options as\n    <a href="#Collection-remove">\n     remove\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-slice">\n    <b class="header">\n     slice\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.slice(begin, end)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Return a shallow copy of this collection\'s models, using the same options as\n      native\n    <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/slice">\n     Array#slice\n    </a>\n    .\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-length">\n    <b class="header">\n     length\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.length\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Like an array, a Collection maintains a\n    <tt>\n     length\n    </tt>\n    property, counting\n      the number of models it contains.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-comparator">\n    <b class="header">\n     comparator\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.comparator\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    By default there is no\n    <b>\n     comparator\n    </b>\n    for a collection.\n      If you define a comparator, it will be used to maintain\n      the collection in sorted order. This means that as models are added,\n      they are inserted at the correct index in\n    <tt>\n     collection.models\n    </tt>\n    .\n      A comparator can be defined as a\n    <a href="http://underscorejs.org/#sortBy">\n     sortBy\n    </a>\n    (pass a function that takes a single argument),\n      as a\n    <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Array/sort">\n     sort\n    </a>\n    (pass a comparator function that expects two arguments),\n      or as a string indicating the attribute to sort by.\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    "sortBy" comparator functions take a model and return a numeric or string\n      value by which the model should be ordered relative to others.\n      "sort" comparator functions take two models, and return\n    <tt>\n     -1\n    </tt>\n    if\n      the first model should come before the second,\n    <tt>\n     0\n    </tt>\n    if they are of\n      the same rank and\n    <tt>\n     1\n    </tt>\n    if the first model should come after.\n    <i>\n     Note that Backbone depends on the arity of your comparator function to\n      determine between the two styles, so be careful if your comparator function\n      is bound.\n    </i>\n   </p>\n   <p>\n    Note how even though all of the chapters in this example are added backwards,\n      they come out in the proper order:\n   </p>\n   <div class="run" title="Run">\n   </div>\n   <pre class="runnable">var Chapter  = Backbone.Model;\nvar chapters = new Backbone.Collection;\n\nchapters.comparator = \'page\';\n\nchapters.add(new Chapter({page: 9, title: "The End"}));\nchapters.add(new Chapter({page: 5, title: "The Middle"}));\nchapters.add(new Chapter({page: 1, title: "The Beginning"}));\n\nalert(chapters.pluck(\'title\'));\n</pre>\n   <p class="warning">\n    Collections with a comparator will not automatically re-sort if you\n      later change model attributes, so you may wish to call\n    <tt>\n     sort\n    </tt>\n    after changing model attributes that would affect the order.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-sort">\n    <b class="header">\n     sort\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.sort([options])\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Force a collection to re-sort itself. You don\'t need to call this under\n      normal circumstances, as a collection with a\n    <a href="#Collection-comparator">\n     comparator\n    </a>\n    will sort itself whenever a model is added. To disable sorting when adding\n      a model, pass\n    <tt>\n     {sort: false}\n    </tt>\n    to\n    <tt>\n     add\n    </tt>\n    . Calling\n    <b>\n     sort\n    </b>\n    triggers a\n    <tt>\n     "sort"\n    </tt>\n    event on the collection.\n   </p>\n   <p id="Collection-pluck">\n    <b class="header">\n     pluck\n    </b>\n    <code>\n     collection.pluck(attribute)\n    </code>\n    <br/>\n    Pluck an attribute from each model in the collection.
